# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Overview

**Task ID**: javascript_web_social_expert_073_architectural_understanding_expert_01
**Category**: architectural_understanding
**Difficulty**: expert
**Language**: javascript
**Context Length**: 739599 tokens
**Files**: 87

## Task Title

Analyze Performance Bottleneck in Asynchronous User Progress Update Flow

## Description

The PulseLearn Campus Hub is a complex, microservices-based e-learning platform. The architecture leverages event-driven patterns using Kafka to ensure services are loosely coupled and scalable, as detailed in the project's Architectural Decision Records (ADRs). Recently, users have reported a significant and intermittent delay: after they complete a course lecture or quiz, it can sometimes take up to a minute for their progress to be reflected on their main dashboard's progress chart and activity stream. This delay is causing user frustration and appears to worsen during peak usage hours. As an expert architect, you need to analyze the system to identify the likely cause of this latency.

## Your Task

Your task is to perform a root cause analysis of the user progress update latency. You must not write or modify any code. Instead, produce a detailed architectural analysis report in markdown format. 

The report must:
1.  **Trace the complete, end-to-end data flow.** Start from the user's action in the frontend (e.g., completing a lecture in `LecturePlayer.js`), through the API Gateway, to all relevant backend services, and finally back to the frontend components that display the progress (`ProgressChart.js`, `ActivityStream.js`). Clearly distinguish between synchronous API calls and asynchronous event-driven messages.
2.  **Identify the key architectural components involved.** List the specific services, databases, message brokers, and critical code modules (e.g., controllers, services, repositories, event producers/consumers) that participate in this flow.
3.  **Pinpoint the top 3 most likely architectural areas causing the delay.** For each potential bottleneck, provide a detailed justification referencing specific files (e.g., `docker-compose.yml`, `nginx.conf`, service code, or ADRs) and architectural patterns (e.g., eventual consistency, producer/consumer configuration) that support your hypothesis.

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would approach this by systemically tracing the data flow and reasoning about the system's design trade-offs.

1.  **Start at the UI:** Examine `frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js` and its child components like `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js` to see how they fetch data. This will likely lead to `frontend/src/services/courseService.js` or a similar client.
2.  **Trace the 'Write' Path:** Hypothesize that completing a lecture triggers a POST/PUT request. Look in `frontend/src/components/course/LecturePlayer.js` for an API call that updates progress.
3.  **Follow to the Backend:** Trace this API call through the `services/api-gateway/nginx.conf` to its destination, the `course-service`.
4.  **Analyze the Core Service Logic:** Inside `course-service`, inspect the relevant controller (`courseController.js`), service (`courseService.js`), and repository (`courseRepository.js`) to see how the progress update is persisted to its database (`schema.prisma`).
5.  **Identify the Asynchronous Link:** Crucially, the developer must consult the documentation, specifically `docs/ADR/002-event-sourcing-with-kafka.md`, to understand that cross-service communication happens via events. They would then look for an event being published in `course-service` after the database write, likely in `services/course-service/src/events/producer.js`.
6.  **Analyze the 'Read' Path:** Return to the dashboard components. How do they get the updated data? They likely poll the `course-service` periodically for the latest progress. The delay is the time between the 'write' action and the next successful 'read' poll that reflects the new data.
7.  **Synthesize Bottlenecks:** The 'intermittent' and 'under load' nature of the problem strongly points away from simple synchronous code and towards the asynchronous messaging system or infrastructure contention. The expert would identify Kafka as the most likely source of variable delay. They would formulate hypotheses based on common failure modes in event-driven systems: producer performance, broker load, and consumer lag. They would also consider the frontend polling strategy as a contributor to perceived latency.

## Evaluation Criteria

- **Flow Tracing Accuracy:** Correctly identifies and separates the synchronous write, asynchronous event, and frontend read paths.
- **Component Identification:** Accurately lists the critical services, infrastructure, and specific files involved in the process.
- **Evidence-Based Reasoning:** Cites specific files (`docker-compose.yml`, ADRs, service code) to justify conclusions.
- **Problem Diagnosis:** Correctly identifies the asynchronous, event-driven nature of the architecture (`eventual consistency`) as the root cause of the *type* of delay.
- **Bottleneck Plausibility:** Proposes at least two plausible, architecturally-sound bottlenecks (e.g., Kafka contention, frontend polling, DB load).
- **Understanding of Trade-offs:** Demonstrates an understanding that this latency is a trade-off inherent in the chosen loosely-coupled, event-driven architecture.

    21→

    23→|------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
    24→| Data-coupling                       | Multiple bounded contexts write to the same tables, causing noisy merge conflicts. |

    30→

55-usertool_resultRead
     1→<!--
     2→  ADR 003: Polyglot Persistence
     3→  PulseLearn Campus Hub
     4→  Status: Accepted
     5→  Date: 2024-05-28
     6→-->
     7→
     8→# 003 – Polyglot Persistence  
     9→
    10→## Status  
    11→Accepted – The decision has been implemented in `v1.4.0`.
    12→
    13→## Context  
    14→PulseLearn Campus Hub is an event-driven system with a variety of read/write patterns:
    15→
    16→* Write-intensive, append-only domain events (≈8 k eps peak)  
    17→* Read-heavy social timelines that must fan-out to thousands of users in < 150 ms  
    18→* Strongly-consistent, relational data for billing, LMS compliance, and audit logs  
    19→* Full-text search over course content and peer-review comments  
    20→* Graph-style traversals for cohort relationships and content recommendations
    21→
    22→A single storage engine cannot optimize for all these needs without unacceptable trade-offs in performance, cost, or developer productivity. We therefore evaluated several strategies:
    23→
    24→| Option | Pros | Cons |
    25→| ------ | ---- | ---- |
    26→| 1. Single SQL RDBMS (PostgreSQL) | ACID, mature tooling | Hot partitions, expensive scaling, poor search |
    27→| 2. Single document DB (MongoDB) | Flexible schema, good read scaling | Event ordering issues, multi-doc transactions slower |
    28→| 3. Polyglot persistence *(selected)* | Fit-for-purpose stores, cost-effective | Operational complexity, cross-store transactions |
    29→
    30→## Decision  
    31→We adopt **polyglot persistence**: each bounded context chooses the persistence technology that best serves its needs, within guardrails enforced by the Platform Team.
    32→
    33→1. **Event Store**  
    34→   *Technology:* Apache Kafka (log), TimescaleDB (cold storage)  
 
... (truncated)

     2→# PulseLearn Campus Hub · Auth Service
     3→
     4→The **Auth Service** is a standalone micro-service that handles:
     5→
     6→* Secure user registration & login (local + social OAuth)
     7→* Stateless JWT authentication with encrypted refresh tokens
     8→* Granular session management and forced log-out
     9→* Role-based authorization (student / mentor / admin)
    10→* Domain-event emission over NATS → `UserRegistered`, `SessionExpired`, …
    11→* Audit-ready logging and metrics (Prometheus)
    12→
    13→The snippets below provide a **complete, runnable reference implementation** that you can paste into the `services/auth-service` folder and start with `npm start`.

65-usertool_resultRead
     1→```markdown
     2→# 📚 PulseLearn Campus Hub – Course Service
     3→
     4→The **Course Service** is a stateless, event-driven micro-service that owns the **Course** aggregate in the PulseLearn ecosystem.  
     5→Its responsibilities include:
     6→
     7→* CRUD life-cycle of courses, modules, and lessons
     8→* Cohort enrolment & role management (student / instructor / TA)
     9→* Publishing domain events (`CourseCreated`, `ModuleUpdated`, `EnrollmentRevoked`, …)
    10→* Consuming cross-cutting events (e.g., `UserDeleted`, `PaymentCaptured`)
    11→* Exposing a REST/JSON API for the web/mobile front-ends
    12→* Persisting data in PostgreSQL via Prisma ORM
    13→* Emitting real-time WebSocket updates to subscribed clients (via the Gateway)
    14→
    15→> TL;DR — **The Course Service is the single source of truth for all course metadata in PulseLearn.**
    16→
    17→
    18→---
    19→
    20→## ✨ Quick Start
    21→
    22→```bash
    23→# 1. Install dependencies
    24→pnpm i
    25→
    26→# 2. Start PostgreSQL & NATS dev stack (via docker-compose)
    27→pnpm docker:up
    28→
    29→# 3. Run DB migrations & seed fixtures
    30→pnpm db:migrate   # => prisma migrate deploy
    31→pnpm db:seed      # => prisma db seed
    32→
    33→# 4. Start the micro-service
    34→pnpm dev
    35→```
    36→
    37→The service boots on `http://localhost:5001` (REST) and connects to NATS at `nats://localhost:4222` by default.
    38→
    39→---
    40→
    41→## 🗂️ Folder Structure
    42→```
    43→services/
    44→└─ course-service/
    45→   ├─ src/
    46→   │  ├─ api/               # Express routers & OpenAPI docs

118-assistanttool_useRead
119-usertool_resultRead
     1→<!--
     2→  ADR 003: Polyglot Persistence
     3→  PulseLearn Campus Hub
     4→  Status: Accepted
     5→  Date: 2024-05-28
     6→-->
     7→
     8→# 003 – Polyglot Persistence  
     9→
    10→## Status  
    11→Accepted – The decision has been implemented in `v1.4.0`.
    12→
    13→## Context  
    14→PulseLearn Campus Hub is an event-driven system with a variety of read/write patterns:
    15→
    16→* Write-intensive, append-only domain events (≈8 k eps peak)  
    17→* Read-heavy social timelines that must fan-out to thousands of users in < 150 ms  
    18→* Strongly-consistent, relational data for billing, LMS compliance, and audit logs  
    19→* Full-text search over course content and peer-review comments  
    20→* Graph-style traversals for cohort relationships and content recommendations
    21→
    22→A single storage engine cannot optimize for all these needs without unacceptable trade-offs in performance, cost, or developer productivity. We therefore evaluated several strategies:
    23→
    24→| Option | Pros | Cons |
    25→| ------ | ---- | ---- |
    26→| 1. Single SQL RDBMS (PostgreSQL) | ACID, mature tooling | Hot partitions, expensive scaling, poor search |
    27→| 2. Single document DB (MongoDB) | Flexible schema, good read scaling | Event ordering issues, multi-doc transactions slower |
    28→| 3. Polyglot persistence *(selected)* | Fit-for-purpose stores, cost-effective | Operational complexity, cross-store transactions |
    29→
    30→## Decision  
    31→We adopt **polyglot persistence**: each bounded context chooses the persistence technology that best serves its needs, within guardrails enforced by the Platform Team.
    32→
    33→1. **Event Store**  
    34→   *Technology:* Apache Kafka (log), TimescaleDB (cold storage)  
 
... (truncated)

123-assistanttext-
I have completed the architectural analysis report. Let me provide a summary of the key findings:

## Summary

I've analyzed the PulseLearn Campus Hub codebase and produced a comprehensive architectural analysis report at `/logs/agent/solution.md`. Here are the key findings:

### Data Flow Overview

The user progress update involves three distinct paths:
1. **Synchronous Write Path**: `LecturePlayer.js` → API Gateway → `course-service` → PostgreSQL + Kafka publish
2. **Asynchronous Event Propagation**: Kafka topics → Multiple consumers (gamification, notification, activity services)
3. **Frontend Read Path**: DashboardPage (REST + WebSocket), ProgressChart (dedicated WebSocket), ActivityStream (hybrid)

### Top 3 Bottlenecks Identified

1. **Kafka Consumer Lag Under Load** (`docker-compose.yml:120-138`, `services/course-service/src/app.js:96`)
   - Single broker with `REPLICATION_FACTOR: 1` creates partition bottlenecks
   - No explicit partitioning strategy leads to hot partitions
   - Consumer groups don't scale horizontally under the current configuration

2. **Frontend Polling Strategy and Stale Cache** (`frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js:139-156`, `frontend/src/services/courseService.js:77-78`)
   - Dashboard only fetches on mount - no periodic polling
   - 30-second TTL cache in courseService returns stale data
   - Multiple uncoordinated WebSocket connections (Socket.io vs native WebSocket)

3. **Eventual Consistency Projection Delay** (`docs/ADR/002-event-sourcing-with-kafka.md`, `docs/ADR/003-polyglot-persistence.md`)
   - Multi-hop event chains (`LESSON_COMPLETED` → `CourseProgressUpdated`)
   - Read models are projections updated asynchronously by consumers
   - Each hop adds latency from processing + network round-trips

### Key Insight

The latency is **n

ARCHITECTURE DECISIONS (ADRs)\n\n### ADR 001 - Microservices Architecture\n**Location:** `/app/project/docs/ADR/001-microservices-architecture.md`\n\n- **Status:** Accepted\n- **Date:** 2024-05-19\n- **Decision:** Event-driven microservices with domain-oriented bounded contexts\n- **Key Points:**\n  - Each service owns its database (Database per Service pattern)\n  - Asynchronous communication via Kafka/NATS\n  - CloudEvents 1.0 spec for event format\n  - Topic naming: `pl.<boundedContext>.<eventName>.<version>`\n  - Shared `@pl/platform` library for event bus abstraction\n  - Saga pattern for distributed transactions\n  - SPIFFE IDs for zero-trust service identity\n  - OpenTelemetry for distributed tracing\n\n### ADR 002 - Event Sourcing with Kafka\n**Location:** `/app/project/docs/ADR/002-event-sourcing-with-kafka.md`\n\n- **Status:** Accepted\n- **Date:** 2024-05-13\n- **Decision:** Kafka as persistent event store and message bus\n- **Key Points:**\n  - Immutable event log as single source of truth\n  - Per-bounded-context topics (e.g., `education.assignment`, `identity.session`)\n  - Schema Registry for versioned schemas\n  - Exactly-once semantics via idempotent producers\n  - Snapshot strategy for long-lived aggregates\n  - Transactional Outbox pattern for atomicity\n  - Event versioning via `schemaVersion` field\n  - Consumer projections for read models\n\n### ADR 003 - Polyglot Persistence\n**Location:** `/app/project/docs/ADR/003-polyglot-persistence.md`\n\n- **Status:** Accepted\n- **Date:** 2024-05-28\n- **Decision:** Use fit-for-purpose datastores within architectural guardrails\n- **Datastore Selection:**\n  1. **Kafka** - Event store and log (immutable, temporal queries)\n  2. **PostgreSQL 15** - User, billing, audit logs (ACID, GDPR)\n  3. **Redis Cluster** - Timelines, notifications, sessions (sub-ms fan-out)\n  4. **OpenSearch 2.x** - Search & analytics (relevance, aggregations)\n  5. **Neo4j 5.x** - Graph recommendations (student relationships)\n  6. **S3/MinIO** - File storage (assignments, media)\n- **Cross-store Sync:** Kafka projection topics for eventual consistency\n- **Pattern:** Repository abstraction layer shields business logic from vendor SDKs\n\n---\n\n## 6. DOMAIN EVENTS & MESSAGE FLOW\n\n### Key Domain Events\n| Event | Payload | Trigger | Consumers |\n|-------|---------|---------|-----------|\n| `CourseCreated` | courseId, ownerId | POST /courses | Achievement Service, Search Indexer |\n| `CoursePublished` | courseId, timestamp | PATCH /courses/:id/publish | Notification Service |\n| `EnrollmentAdded` | courseId, userId, role | User enrolls in course | Notification, Gamification Services |\n| `AssignmentSubmitted` | assignmentId, userId, fileUrl | Student uploads assignment | Gamification Service (points), Badge Service |\n| `BadgeAwarded` | badgeId, userId, reason | Gamification decision | Dashboard updates via WebSocket |\n| `SessionExpired` | userId, expiresAt | JWT TTL expiration | Cleanup services |\n| `LectureUploaded` | lectureId, courseId | Instructor uploads content | Search indexing, CDN delivery |\n| `CoursePaid` | orderId, userId, amount | Stripe webhook | Enrollment activation, Invoice generation |\n\n### Event Flow Pattern\n1. **Producer:** Service executes command, publishes immutable event to Kafka/NATS\n2. **Event Store:** Kafka log compacts and replicates events\n3. **Consumers:** Other services subscribe to topics and project read models\n4. **Idempotency:** Consumers use event IDs to prevent duplicate processing\n5. **DLQ:** Poison messages sent to dead-letter queue for manual inspection\n\n---\n\n## 7. 180\u2192\n   181\u2192Each domain action emits an immutable event.  \n   182\u2192Events are versioned, schema-registered, and can be replayed for new projections.\n   183\u2192\n   184\u2192| Event |\n   186\u2192| `AssignmentSubmitted`   | `assignmentId`, `userId`, `file`  | Student uploads assignment       |\n   187\u2192| `BadgeAwarded`          | `badgeId`, `userId`, `reason`     | 206\u2192```\n   207\u2192\n   208\u2192---\n   209\u2192\n   210\u2192## Security & Compliance\n   211\u2192\n   212\u2192* TLS 1.3 enforced end-to-end (Let\u2019s Encrypt in dev, ACM in prod)  \n   213\u2192* Argon2id passwords, JWTs signed with 4096-bit RSA keys  \n   214\u2192* OWASP Top-10 hardened (rate-limiting, input validation via Zod)  \n   215\u2192* GDPR: Right-to-be-Forgotten Context  \n    13\u2192\n    14\u2192PulseLearn Campus Hub (PL-CH) must enable:\n    15\u2192\n    16\u21921. Real-time, bidirectional interactions between thousands of concurrent users (students, teachers, admins).  \n    17\u21922. Rapid feature evolution by autonomous domain-centric teams.  \n    18\u21923. Fault-tolerance and graceful degradation of non-critical functionality (e.g., delayed \u201cBadgeAwarded\u201d events must **not** block quiz submissions).  \n    19\u21924. Polyglot technology choices while enforcing a consistent ops/observability contract.  \n    20\u21925. Compliance with FERPA, GDPR, and internal audit requirements such as end-to-end traceability and PII redaction policies.\n    21\u2192\n    22\u2192The alternatives considered were:\n    23\u2192\n    24\u2192| Candidate                     | Pros                                                                                                    | Cons                                                                                                   |\n    25\u2192| ----------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n    26\u2192| A) Single-service (monolith)  | Simple to deploy, transactional consistency, easier local dev                                           | Scalability bottlenecks, slower team velocity, long-lived branches, risky deployments                  |\n    27\u2192| B) Self-contained services    | Autonomy per bounded context, independent UI + API bundles                                              | Risk of UI duplication, heavier front-end orchestration                                                |\n    28\u2192| **C) Microservices + Event Bus** | Loose coupling via events, horizontal scalability, team autonomy, tech polyglot, easier domain modeling | Requires distributed tracing, eventual consistency semantics, operational complexity                   |\n    29\u2192| D) Serverless (FaaS only)     | Zero infra management, cost per execution                                                               | Cold starts, vendor lock-in, limited long-running connections, complex local testing                   |\n    30\u2192\n    31\u2192After evaluating traffic patterns, compliance constraints, and organisation structure (5 cross-functional squads), option **C** was chosen.\n    32\u2192\n    33\u2192---\n    34\u2192\n    35\u2192## 2. Decision  \n    36\u2192\n    37\u2192We will build **PulseLearn Campus Hub** as an **event-driven microservices system**:\n    38\u2192\n    39\u21921. **Domain-Oriented Microservices**  \n    40\u2192   \u2022 Each service owns a bounded context & data store (e.g., `UserProfile`, `LearningPath`, `Achievement`, `Notification`).  \n    41\u2192   \u2022 Services communicate asynchronously via a Kafka compatible bus (NATS JetStream in staging, Confluent Cloud in prod).  \n    42\u2192   \u2022 REST/gRPC APIs remain for synchronous \u201cquery\u201d use-cases and external integrations (admin panel, LTI).  \n    43\u2192\n    44\u21922. **Event Taxonomy**  \n    45\u2192   \u2022 All domain events adopt the CloudEvents 1.0 spec.  \n    46\u2192   \u2022 Topic naming: `pl.<boundedContext>.<eventName>.<version>` (e.g., `pl.achievement.badge_awarded.v1`).  \n    47\u2192   \u2022 Payloads are validated with versioned Avro schemas stored in Schema Registry.  \n    48\u2192\n    49\u21923. **Shared Platform Libraries**  \n    50\u2192   \u2022 We ship an OSS-friendly **`@pl/platform`** JavaScript package that wraps NATS/Kafka producers & consumers, tracing, and idempotency utilities (see snippet below).  \n    51\u2192   \u2022 Analogous libraries will exist for Python, Go, and Java to keep polyglot parity.  \n    52\u2192\n    53\u21924. **Observability & Resilience**  \n    54\u2192   \u2022 OpenTelemetry for distributed tracing, correlated logs, metrics (`traceId` + `spanId` pass via W3C `traceparent`).  \n    55\u2192   \u2022 Circuit breakers (opossum) guard cross-service HTTP calls.  \n    56\u2192   \u2022 Retry, DLQ, and \u201cparking lot\u201d patterns for poison messages.  \n    57\u2192\n    58\u21925. **Security**  \n    59\u2192   \u2022 mTLS between services (Linkerd service mesh).  \n    60\u2192   \u2022 SPIFFE IDs for zero-trust identity.  \n    61\u2192   \u2022 PII encrypted at rest (PostgreSQL + envelope encryption).  \n    62\u2192\n    63\u2192---\n    64\u2192\n    65\u2192## 3. Consequences  \n    66\u2192\n    67\u2192Positive:  \n    68\u2192\u2713 Independent deployability enables <15 min release cadence per squad.  \n    69\u2192\u2713 Horizontal scaling by workload (e.g., `RecommendationService` auto-scales via KEDA based on Kafka lag).  \n    70\u2192\u2713 Failure isolation\u2014`SearchIndexer` crash has no direct impact on \u201cQuizCompletion\u201d UX.  \n    71\u2192\n    72\u2192Negative:  \n    73\u2192\u2717 Added operational overhead: CI/CD pipelines, playbooks, Terraform modules per service.  \n    74\u2192\u2717 Data consistency becomes eventual; we must adopt Saga patterns for workflows like \u201cPurchaseCourse \u2192 ActivateAccess \u2192 EmitInvoice\u201d.  \n    75\u2192\u2717 On-call complexity: PagerDuty rotations per squad, plus a shared SRE roster for platform components (Kafka, Linkerd, Istio ingress).\n    76\u2192\n    77\u2192---\n    78\u2192\n    79\u2192## 4. Implementation Sketch  \n    80\u2192\n    81\u2192### Mermaid: High-level view\n    82\u2192\n    83\u2192```mermaid\n    84\u2192flowchart LR\n    85\u2192    subgraph Frontend\n    86\u2192        ReactApp[Web SPA]\n    87\u2192        MobileApp[React Native]\n    88\u2192    end\n    89\u2192    ReactApp -->|REST: /api/v1| APIGateway\n    90\u2192    MobileApp -->|GraphQL| APIGateway\n    91\u2192    APIGateway --> AuthSvc[(Auth Service)]\n    92\u2192    APIGateway --> UserSvc[(User Profile)]\n    93\u2192    APIGateway --> CourseSvc[(Course Catalog)]\n    94\u2192    style APIGateway fill:#f5f5f5,stroke:#333,stroke-width:1px\n    95\u2192    \n    96\u2192    %% Event Bus\n    97\u2192    subgraph EventBus[\"NATS / Kafka\"]\n    98\u2192        NATS[(JetStream Topic)]\n    99\u2192    end\n   100\u2192    \n   101\u2192    CourseSvc -->|pl.course.uploaded| NATS\n   102\u2192    UserSvc -->|pl.user.session_expired| NATS\n   103\u2192    NATS --> SearchSvc[(Search Indexer)]\n   104\u2192    NATS --> BadgeSvc[(Achievement)]\n   105\u2192    NATS --> RecSvc[(Recommendation)]\n   106\u2192```\n   107\u2192\n   108\u2192### Shared JS Event Library (`@pl/platform`)\n   109\u2192\n   110\u2192```javascript\n   111\u2192// @pl/platform/lib/event-bus.js\n   112\u2192import { connect, StringCodec } from 'nats';\n   113\u2192import { v4 as uuid } from 'uuid';\n   114\u2192import * as otel from '@opentelemetry/api';\n   115\u2192\n   116\u2192/**\n   117\u2192 * EventBus singleton to publish/subscribe CloudEvents-compliant messages.\n   118\u2192 */\n   119\u2192export class EventBus {\n   120\u2192  static instance;\n   121\u2192\n   122\u2192  /**\n   123\u2192   * Initialise a NATS connection (lazy).\n   124\u2192   * @param {object} config - {servers: string, jwt?: string, nkey?: string}\n   125\u2192   */\n   126\u2192  static async init(config) {\n   127\u2192    if (!EventBus.instance) {\n   128\u2192      EventBus.instance = new EventBus(config);\n   129\u2192      await EventBus.instance._connect();\n   130\u2192    }\n   131\u2192    return EventBus.instance;\n   132\u2192  }\n   133\u2192\n   134\u2192  constructor(config) {\n   135\u2192    this.config = config;\n   136\u2192    this.sc = StringCodec();\n   137\u2192  }\n   138\u2192\n   139\u2192  async _connect() {\n   140\u2192    try {\n   141\u2192      this.nc = await connect(this.config);\n   142\u2192      this.js = this.nc.jetstream();\n   143\u2192      console.info('[EventBus] Connected to NATS');\n   144\u2192    } catch (err) {\n   145\u2192      console.error('[EventBus] Connection error', err);\n   146\u2192      throw err;\n   147\u2192    }\n   148\u2192  }\n   149\u2192\n   150\u2192  /**\n   151\u2192   * Publish a CloudEvent to the given topic.\n   152\u2192   * @param {string} topic - e.g. \"pl.achievement.badge_awarded.v1\"\n   153\u2192   * @param {object} data - event payload\n   154\u2192   * @param {object} [options] - headers, trace context, etc.\n   155\u2192   */\n   156\u2192  async publish(topic, data, options = {}) {\n   157\u2192    if (!this.nc) throw new Error('EventBus not initialised');\n   158\u2192    const span = otel.trace.getTracer('pl-platform').startSpan(`publish:${topic}`);\n   159\u2192    try {\n   160\u2192      const event = {\n   161\u2192        id: uuid(),\n   162\u2192        source: 'pulselearn-campus-hub',\n   163\u2192        specversion: '1.0',\n   164\u2192        type: topic,\n   165\u2192        time: new Date().toISOString(),\n   166\u2192        datacontenttype: 'application/json',\n   167\u2192        data,\n   168\u2192      };\n   169\u2192      // propagate trace context\n   170\u2192      const headers = this._buildHeaders(span, options.headers);\n   171\u2192      await this.js.publish(topic, this.sc.encode(JSON.stringify(event)), { headers });\n   172\u2192      span.setStatus({ code: otel.SpanStatusCode.OK });\n   173\u2192    } catch (err) {\n   174\u2192      span.setStatus({ code: otel.SpanStatusCode.ERROR, message: err.message });\n   175\u2192      throw err;\n   176\u2192    } finally {\n   177\u2192      span.end();\n   178\u2192    }\n   179\u2192  }\n   180\u2192\n   181\u2192  /**\n   182\u2192   * Subscribe to a topic with durable consumer semantics.\n   183\u2192   * @param {string} topic\n   184\u2192   * @param {string} durableName\n   185\u2192   * @param {(evt: object) => Promise<void>} handler\n   186\u2192   */\n   187\u2192  async subscribe(topic, durableName, handler) {\n   188\u2192    const subOpts = { durable: durableName, manualAck: true, ackWait: 60_000 };\n   189\u2192    const sub = await this.js.subscribe(topic, subOpts);\n   190\u2192    console.info(`[EventBus] Subscribed to ${topic}`);\n   191\u2192\n   192\u2192    (async () => {\n   193\u2192      for await (const m of sub) {\n   194\u2192        const span = otel.trace.getTracer('pl-platform').startSpan(`consume:${topic}`);\n   195\u2192        try {\n   196\u2192          const evt = JSON.parse(this.sc.decode(m.data));\n   197\u2192          await handler(evt);\n   198\u2192          m.ack();\n   199\u2192          span.setStatus({ code: otel.SpanStatusCode.OK });\n   200\u2192        } catch (err) {\n   201\u2192          console.error('[EventBus] Handler error', err);\n   202\u2192          // let JetStream redeliver, or add to DLQ via a header\n   203\u2192          span.setStatus({ code: otel.SpanStatusCode.ERROR, message: err.message });\n   204\u2192        } finally {\n   205\u2192          span.end();\n   206\u2192        }\n   207\u2192      }\n   208\u2192    })().catch((err) => console.error('[EventBus] Async iteration error', err));\n   209\u2192  }\n   210\u2192\n   211\u2192  _buildHeaders(span, extra = {}) {\n   212\u2192    const headers = this.nc.headers();\n   213\u2192    const ctx = otel.trace.setSpan(otel.context.active(), span);\n   214\u2192    otel.propagation.inject(ctx, headers, {\n   215\u2192      set: (carrier, key, value) => carrier.set(key, value),\n   216\u2192    });\n   217\u2192    Object.entries(extra).forEach(([k, v]) => headers.set(k, v));\n   218\u2192    return headers;\n   219\u2192  }\n   220\u2192}\n   221\u2192```\n   222\u2192\n   223\u2192### Saga Orchestration Example (Enroll Premium Course)\n   224\u2192\n   225\u2192```javascript\n   226\u2192// services/payment/src/enrollCourseSaga.js\n   227\u2192import { EventBus } from '@pl/platform';\n   228\u2192import { db } from '../db';\n   229\u2192import { generateInvoice } from '../billing';\n   230\u2192import { logger } from '../logger';\n   231\u2192\n   232\u2192export async function registerEventHandlers() {\n   233\u2192  const bus = await EventBus.init({ servers: process.env.NATS_URL });\n   234\u2192\n   235\u2192  // listen to PaymentCaptured\n   236\u2192  await bus.subscribe('pl.payment.captured.v1', 'enroll-premium-course', async (evt) => {\n   237\u2192    const { userId, courseId, paymentId } = evt.data;\n   238\u2192    logger.info('Payment captured', { userId, courseId, paymentId });\n   239\u2192\n   240\u2192    // Step 1: Activate access in course service (synchronous call)\n   241\u2192    try {\n   242\u2192      await activateCourseAccess(userId, courseId);\n   243\u2192    } catch (err) {\n   244\u2192      logger.error('Course activation failed', err);\n   245\u2192      // emit compensating event\n   246\u2192      await bus.publish('pl.payment.refund_requested.v1', { paymentId, reason: 'COURSE_ACTIVATION_FAILED' });\n   247\u2192      return;\n   248\u2192    }\n   249\u2192\n   250\u2192    // Step 2: Emit EnrollmentGranted event\n   251\u2192    await bus.publish('pl.enrollment.granted.v1', { userId, courseId });\n   252\u2192\n   253\u2192    // Step 3: Issue invoice (local DB + external PDF generator)\n   254\u2192    try {\n   255\u2192      const invoiceId = await generateInvoice({ userId, paymentId });\n   256\u2192      await db.invoice.markSent(invoiceId);\n   257\u2192    } catch (err) {\n   258\u2192      logger.error('Invoice generation failed', err);\n   259\u2192      // Non-blocking; instructor & finance will be alerted via DLQ consumer\n   260\u2192    }\n   261\u2192  });\n   262\u2192}\n   263\u2192```\n   264\u2192\n   265\u2192---\n   266\u2192\n   267\u2192## 5. Alternatives Explored (But NOT Chosen)\n   268\u2192\n   269\u2192* **Monolith + Event Module** \u2013 insufficient isolation; high coordination cost for multi-squad development.  \n   270\u2192* **Pure Serverless** \u2013 latency and unpredictable cost for high-frequency message streams (quizzes, edits).  \n   271\u2192* **gRPC-only Service Mesh** \u2013 synchronous coupling failed chaos testing when `AnalyticsService` induced 40 % error rate.\n   272\u2192\n   273\u2192---\n   274\u2192\n   275\u2192## 6. Validation & Next Steps\n   276\u2192\n   277\u21921. Platform Team to spin up NATS + JetStream in staging (k8s operator).  \n   278\u21922. Each squad migrates at least one bounded context to the new pattern by Sprint 14.  \n   279\u21923. Evaluate Confluent vs Redpanda for prod by Q3.  \n   280\u21924. Conduct load test: 50k concurrent websocket sessions, publish 2k events/s, < 200 ms P99 end-to-end latency.  \n   281\u2192\n   282\u2192---\n   283\u2192\n   284\u2192## 7. References\n   285\u2192\n   286\u2192* \u201cBuilding Event-Driven Microservices\u201d \u2013 O\u2019Reilly, 2021  \n   287\u2192* CloudEvents 1.0 Spec \u2013 https://cloudevents.io/  \n   288\u2192* JetStream Acknowledgements \u2013 https://docs.nats.io/jetstream/consumers/ack_policy  \n   289\u2192* Saga Pattern \u2013 https://microservices.io/patterns/data/saga.html  \n   290\u2192\n   291\u2192```\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. "     1\u2192```markdown\n     2\u2192# ADR-002: Introduce Event Sourcing with Kafka\n     3\u2192\n     4\u2192* Status: **Accepted**  \n     5\u2192* Date: 2024-05-13  \n     6\u2192* Decision Makers: Core Platform Team (PulseLearn Campus Hub)  \n     7\u2192* Supersedes: *N/A*  \n     8\u2192* References: PCH-RFC-11, ADR-001 (Adopt Micro-Service Architecture)  \n     9\u2192\n    10\u2192---\n    11\u2192\n    12\u2192## 1. Context \u2011 Why change?\n    13\u2192\n    14\u2192PulseLearn Campus Hub (PCH) is experiencing rapid feature growth:\n    15\u2192\n    16\u2192* Real-time dashboards for quiz progress, peer-review feedback, and badge awards  \n    17\u2192* A new gamification engine that recalculates points on every learning event  \n    18\u2192* Audit-ready reporting for compliance and accreditation bodies  \n    19\u2192\n    20\u2192The existing CRUD-centric model has hit several limits:\n    21\u2192\n    22\u2192| Pain-Point                          | Symptom                                                                             |\n    23\u2192|------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n    24\u2192| Data-coupling                       | Multiple bounded contexts write to the same tables, causing noisy merge conflicts. |\n    25\u2192| Missed notifications                | Lost WebSocket messages because they were dispatched directly from HTTP handlers.   |\n    26\u2192| Operational complexity              | Replaying history (e.g., to debug ranking errors) requires fragile SQL scripts.     |\n    27\u2192| Lack of temporal data               | Hard to answer \u201cWhat was Alice\u2019s score at 14:01 yesterday?\u201d                         |\n    28\u2192\n    29\u2192To address these, we want:\n    30\u2192\n    31\u21921. **Immutable event log** \u2013 the single source of truth  \n    32\u21922. **Replayability** \u2013 rebuild read-models at any point in time  \n    33\u21923. **Loose coupling** \u2013 services subscribe to what they need, when they need it  \n    34\u21924. **Scalability** \u2013 horizontal partitioning of event streams  \n    35\u2192\n    36\u2192Apache **Kafka** is already used in our data-analytics pipeline; adopting it as the system event backbone is a natural next step.\n    37\u2192\n    38\u2192---\n    39\u2192\n    40\u2192## 2. Decision\n    41\u2192\n    42\u2192We will adopt **event sourcing** for all new domain workflows and gradually migrate existing ones.  \n    43\u2192Kafka will act as the **persistent event store** (commit log) and **message bus**.  \n    44\u2192Specifics:\n    45\u2192\n    46\u21921. **Each bounded context owns its topic(s)** \u2013 e.g. `education.assignment`, `identity.session`, `gamification.badge`.\n    47\u21922. **Events are immutable** JSON messages, versioned via a `schemaVersion` field; schema registry enforced at the gateway.\n    48\u21923. **Append-only**: write operations emit events; read models are derived via consumer projections.\n    49\u21924. **Exactly-once** semantics: achieved by Kafka idempotent producers + transactional writes to outbox tables when necessary.\n    50\u21925. **Snapshot strategy**: Long-lived aggregates publish `*.snapshot` events every *n* revisions to shorten replay time.\n    51\u21926. **Backward compatibility**: Services must ignore unknown fields and can only add optional fields to existing event versions.\n    52\u2192\n    53\u2192---\n    54\u2192\n    55\u2192## 3. Consequences\n    56\u2192\n    57\u2192Positive:\n    58\u2192\n    59\u2192* **Auditability** \u2013 every state change is traceable.  \n    60\u2192* **Resilience** \u2013 consumers can restart and replay without data loss.  \n    61\u2192* **Scalable read models** \u2013 each service builds its own query-optimized projection.  \n    62\u2192\n    63\u2192Negative / Trade-offs:\n    64\u2192\n    65\u2192* **Write complexity** \u2013 commands must succeed or be compensated by new events.  \n    66\u2192* **Learning curve** \u2013 developers must understand eventual consistency.  \n    67\u2192* **Storage cost** \u2013 Kafka cluster size grows with retained history.  \n    68\u2192\n    69\u2192---\n    70\u2192\n    71\u2192## 4. Implementation Sketch (JavaScript / Node.js)\n    72\u2192\n    73\u2192Below are cut-down excerpts from production code to guide contributors.  \n    74\u2192All examples assume Node.js \u2265 18, TypeScript, and the `kafkajs` client.\n    75\u2192\n    76\u2192### 4.1 Common Infrastructure\n    77\u2192\n    78\u2192```ts\n    79\u2192// src/infrastructure/kafka/kafkaClient.ts\n    80\u2192import { Kafka, logLevel } from 'kafkajs';\n    81\u2192import config from '../../config';\n    82\u2192\n    83\u2192export const kafka = new Kafka({\n    84\u2192  clientId: 'pulselearn-campus-hub',\n    85\u2192  brokers : config.kafka.brokers,\n    86\u2192  ssl     : true,\n    87\u2192  sasl    : {\n    88\u2192    mechanism : 'scram-sha-256',\n    89\u2192    username  : config.kafka.username,\n    90\u2192    password  : config.kafka.password,\n    91\u2192  },\n    92\u2192  logLevel: logLevel.WARN,\n    93\u2192});\n    94\u2192\n    95\u2192export function topicName(boundedContext: string, suffix = ''): string {\n    96\u2192  return `${config.env}.${boundedContext}${suffix && `.${suffix}`}`;\n    97\u2192}\n    98\u2192```\n    99\u2192\n   100\u2192### 4.2 Event Contracts\n   101\u2192\n   102\u2192```ts\n   103\u2192// src/domain/events/AssignmentSubmittedEvent.ts\n   104\u2192import { z } from 'zod';\n   105\u2192\n   106\u2192export const AssignmentSubmittedEventSchema = z.object({\n   107\u2192  schemaVersion  : z.literal(1),\n   108\u2192  eventId        : z.string().uuid(),\n   109\u2192  aggregateId    : z.string().uuid(),   // Assignment ID\n   110\u2192  type           : z.literal('AssignmentSubmitted'),\n   111\u2192  occurredAt     : z.string().datetime({ offset: true }),\n   112\u2192  payload        : z.object({\n   113\u2192    courseId  : z.string().uuid(),\n   114\u2192    studentId : z.string().uuid(),\n   115\u2192    fileUrl   : z.string().url(),\n   116\u2192  }),\n   117\u2192});\n   118\u2192\n   119\u2192export type AssignmentSubmittedEvent = z.infer<typeof AssignmentSubmittedEventSchema>;\n   120\u2192```\n   121\u2192\n   122\u2192### 4.3 Producer (Command Handler -> Event)\n   123\u2192\n   124\u2192```ts\n   125\u2192// src/application/commands/submitAssignment.ts\n   126\u2192import { AssignmentSubmittedEvent } from '../../domain/events/AssignmentSubmittedEvent';\n   127\u2192import { kafka, topicName } from '../../infrastructure/kafka/kafkaClient';\n   128\u2192import { randomUUID } from 'crypto';\n   129\u2192\n   130\u2192export async function submitAssignment(cmd: {\n   131\u2192  courseId: string;\n   132\u2192  studentId: string;\n   133\u2192  fileUrl: string;\n   134\u2192}): Promise<void> {\n   135\u2192  // Business validation omitted for brevity\n   136\u2192\n   137\u2192  const event: AssignmentSubmittedEvent = {\n   138\u2192    schemaVersion : 1,\n   139\u2192    eventId       : randomUUID(),\n   140\u2192    aggregateId   : randomUUID(),\n   141\u2192    type          : 'AssignmentSubmitted',\n   142\u2192    occurredAt    : new Date().toISOString(),\n   143\u2192    payload       : cmd,\n   144\u2192  };\n   145\u2192\n   146\u2192  const producer = kafka.producer({ idempotent: true });\n   147\u2192  await producer.connect();\n   148\u2192\n   149\u2192  try {\n   150\u2192    await producer.send({\n   151\u2192      topic: topicName('education.assignment'),\n   152\u2192      messages: [\n   153\u2192        {\n   154\u2192          key  : event.aggregateId,\n   155\u2192          value: JSON.stringify(event),\n   156\u2192          headers: {\n   157\u2192            'schema-version': '1',\n   158\u2192            'event-type'    : event.type,\n   159\u2192          },\n   160\u2192        },\n   161\u2192      ],\n   162\u2192    });\n   163\u2192  } finally {\n   164\u2192    await producer.disconnect();\n   165\u2192  }\n   166\u2192}\n   167\u2192```\n   168\u2192\n   169\u2192### 4.4 Consumer Projection (Gamification Points)\n   170\u2192\n   171\u2192```ts\n   172\u2192// src/projections/gamification/pointsProjector.ts\n   173\u2192import { kafka, topicName } from '../../infrastructure/kafka/kafkaClient';\n   174\u2192import { AssignmentSubmittedEventSchema } from '../../domain/events/AssignmentSubmittedEvent';\n   175\u2192import pointsRepo from '../../repositories/pointsRepository';\n   176\u2192\n   177\u2192export async function runPointsProjector(): Promise<void> {\n   178\u2192  const consumer = kafka.consumer({\n   179\u2192    groupId: 'gamification-points-projector-v1',\n   180\u2192  });\n   181\u2192\n   182\u2192  await consumer.connect();\n   183\u2192  await consumer.subscribe({\n   184\u2192    topic: topicName('education.assignment'),\n   185\u2192    fromBeginning: false,\n   186\u2192  });\n   187\u2192\n   188\u2192  await consumer.run({\n   189\u2192    eachMessage: async ({ message, partition }) => {\n   190\u2192      try {\n   191\u2192        const raw = message.value?.toString() ?? '{}';\n   192\u2192        const parsed = AssignmentSubmittedEventSchema.parse(JSON.parse(raw));\n   193\u2192\n   194\u2192        await pointsRepo.increment(\n   195\u2192          parsed.payload.studentId,\n   196\u2192          /* points = */ 5,\n   197\u2192        );\n   198\u2192\n   199\u2192        console.info(\n   200\u2192          `[PointProjector] +5 for student=${parsed.payload.studentId} (partition=${partition})`,\n   201\u2192        );\n   202\u2192      } catch (err) {\n   203\u2192        // DLQ or retry logic could be implemented here\n   204\u2192        console.error('[PointProjector] Failed to process message', err);\n   205\u2192      }\n   206\u2192    },\n   207\u2192  });\n   208\u2192}\n   209\u2192```\n   210\u2192\n   211\u2192### 4.5 Snapshotter Utility\n   212\u2192\n   213\u2192```ts\n   214\u2192// src/utils/snapshotter.ts\n   215\u2192import { kafka, topicName } from '../infrastructure/kafka/kafkaClient';\n   216\u2192\n   217\u2192export async function publishSnapshot<T>({\n   218\u2192  boundedContext,\n   219\u2192  aggregateName,\n   220\u2192  aggregateId,\n   221\u2192  revision,\n   222\u2192  state,\n   223\u2192}: {\n   224\u2192  boundedContext: string;\n   225\u2192  aggregateName: string;\n   226\u2192  aggregateId: string;\n   227\u2192  revision: number;\n   228\u2192  state: T;\n   229\u2192}): Promise<void> {\n   230\u2192  const producer = kafka.producer();\n   231\u2192\n   232\u2192  await producer.connect();\n   233\u2192  try {\n   234\u2192    await producer.send({\n   235\u2192      topic: topicName(`${boundedContext}.${aggregateName}.snapshot`),\n   236\u2192      messages: [\n   237\u2192        {\n   238\u2192          key  : aggregateId,\n   239\u2192          value: JSON.stringify({\n   240\u2192            schemaVersion: 1,\n   241\u2192            type         : `${aggregateName}.snapshot`,\n   242\u2192            revision,\n   243\u2192            occurredAt   : new Date().toISOString(),\n   244\u2192            state,\n   245\u2192          }),\n   246\u2192        },\n   247\u2192      ],\n   248\u2192    });\n   249\u2192  } finally {\n   250\u2192    await producer.disconnect();\n   251\u2192  }\n   252\u2192}\n   253\u2192```\n   254\u2192\n   255\u2192---\n   256\u2192\n   257\u2192## 5. Migration Path\n   258\u2192\n   259\u21921. **Brown-field integration**: legacy CRUD modules will emit events in a \u201cchange-data-capture\u201d style, then slowly migrate command handling logic.  \n   260\u21922. **Feature toggles**: Read models behind `/v2/` API routes will use event projections; `/v1/` remains on relational reads.  \n   261\u21923. **Runbook & SRE**: New runbooks added for Kafka cluster monitoring (Lag, ISR, Disk usage).  \n   262\u21924. **Developer enablement**: Internal workshop + \u201cEvent Sourcing 101\u201d wiki page.  \n   263\u2192\n   264\u2192---\n   265\u2192\n   266\u2192## 6. Rejected Alternatives\n   267\u2192\n   268\u2192* **RabbitMQ + Outbox pattern** \u2013 flexible routing but lacks strong log-compaction and replay features.  \n   269\u2192* **Full CQRS without Event Sourcing** \u2013 improves reads but doesn\u2019t solve auditability or temporal requirements.  \n   270\u2192\n   271\u2192---\n   272\u2192\n   273\u2192## 7. Open Issues / Next Steps\n   274\u2192\n   275\u21921. Define retention policy per topic (regulatory requirement: 5-year minimum).  \n   276\u21922. Agree on company-wide naming convention for events (`<Domain>.<Action><PastTense>`).  \n   277\u21923. Evaluate Confluent Schema Registry vs. open-source alternatives.  \n   278\u21924. Prototype snapshotting performance with 1M-event aggregate.  \n   279\u2192\n   280\u2192---\n   281\u2192\n   282\u2192> \u201cIf you treat data as immutable facts, your systems become a chronicle of truth, not just a reflection of the present.\u201d \u2013  Tech Lead, PCH\n   283\u2192```\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer questions about the code behavior.\n</system-reminder>\n"

"     1\u2192<!--\n     2\u2192  ADR 003: Polyglot Persistence\n     3\u2192  PulseLearn Campus Hub\n     4\u2192  Status: Accepted\n     5\u2192  Date: 2024-05-28\n     6\u2192-->\n     7\u2192\n     8\u2192# 003 \u2013 Polyglot Persistence  \n     9\u2192\n    10\u2192## Status  \n    11\u2192Accepted \u2013 The decision has been implemented in `v1.4.0`.\n    12\u2192\n    13\u2192## Context  \n    14\u2192PulseLearn Campus Hub is an event-driven system with a variety of read/write patterns:\n    15\u2192\n    16\u2192* Write-intensive, append-only domain events (\u22488 k eps peak)  \n    17\u2192* Read-heavy social timelines that must fan-out to thousands of users in < 150 ms  \n    18\u2192* Strongly-consistent, relational data for billing, LMS compliance, and audit logs  \n    19\u2192* Full-text search over course content and peer-review comments  \n    20\u2192* Graph-style traversals for cohort relationships and content recommendations\n    21\u2192\n    22\u2192A single storage engine cannot optimize for all these needs without unacceptable trade-offs in performance, cost, or developer productivity. We therefore evaluated several strategies:\n    23\u2192\n    24\u2192| Option | Pros | Cons |\n    25\u2192| ------ | ---- | ---- |\n    26\u2192| 1. Single SQL RDBMS (PostgreSQL) | ACID, mature tooling | Hot partitions, expensive scaling, poor search |\n    27\u2192| 2. Single document DB (MongoDB) | Flexible schema, good read scaling | Event ordering issues, multi-doc transactions slower |\n    28\u2192| 3. Polyglot persistence *(selected)* | Fit-for-purpose stores, cost-effective | Operational complexity, cross-store transactions |\n    29\u2192\n    30\u2192## Decision  \n    31\u2192We adopt **polyglot persistence**: each bounded context chooses the persistence technology that best serves its needs, within guardrails enforced by the Platform Team.\n    32\u2192\n    33\u21921. **Event Store**  \n    34\u2192   *Technology:* Apache Kafka (log), TimescaleDB (cold storage)  \n    35\u2192   *Rationale:* Immutability, temporal queries, built-in replication.\n    36\u2192\n    37\u21922. **User & Billing**  \n    38\u2192   *Technology:* PostgreSQL 15 with logical replication  \n    39\u2192   *Rationale:* Strong consistency for payments, GDPR data-subject requests.\n    40\u2192\n    41\u21923. **Realtime Timelines & Notifications**  \n    42\u2192   *Technology:* Redis Cluster + Redis Streams  \n    43\u2192   *Rationale:* Sub-millisecond fan-out, pub/sub semantics, TTL-based eviction.\n    44\u2192\n    45\u21924. **Search & Analytics**  \n    46\u2192   *Technology:* OpenSearch 2.x  \n    47\u2192   *Rationale:* Relevance scoring, aggregations, horizontal scaling.\n    48\u2192\n    49\u21925. **Graph Recommendations**  \n    50\u2192   *Technology:* Neo4j 5.x  \n    51\u2192   *Rationale:* Native graph traversals for \u201cstudents who liked X also liked Y\u201d.\n    52\u2192\n    53\u21926. **File Storage (Assignments, Media)**  \n    54\u2192   *Technology:* S3-compatible object store with signed URLs  \n    55\u2192   *Rationale:* Durable, CDN-friendly, off-loads traffic from app servers.\n    56\u2192\n    57\u2192### Access Pattern Enforcement  \n    58\u2192```mermaid\n    59\u2192graph TD\n    60\u2192  subgraph Service Layer\n    61\u2192    SVC[Micro-service]\n    62\u2192  end\n    63\u2192  subgraph Repositories\n    64\u2192    REPO1[(PostgreSQL Repo)]\n    65\u2192    REPO2[(Redis Repo)]\n    66\u2192    REPO3[(Kafka Repo)]\n    67\u2192  end\n    68\u2192  SVC --> REPO1 & REPO2 & REPO3\n    69\u2192```\n    70\u2192\n    71\u2192Repositories shield business logic from vendor SDKs. All repositories implement:\n    72\u2192\n    73\u2192```ts\n    74\u2192// docs/examples/Repository.ts\n    75\u2192export interface Repository<T> {\n    76\u2192  findById(id: string): Promise<T | null>;\n    77\u2192  save(entity: T): Promise<void>;\n    78\u2192  delete(id: string): Promise<void>;\n    79\u2192}\n    80\u2192```\n    81\u2192\n    82\u2192Concrete adapters (e.g., `UserPgRepository`, `TimelineRedisRepository`) live in their respective packages.\n    83\u2192\n    84\u2192### Data-Contracts & Async Sync  \n    85\u2192Cross-store ownership is disallowed; instead we replicate immutable projections using Kafka topics suffixed with `.projection`. Consumers materialize local read models, guaranteeing eventual consistency while avoiding distributed transactions.\n    86\u2192\n    87\u2192## Consequences  \n    88\u2192Positive\n    89\u2192* Services scale independently; no single datastore becomes a bottleneck.\n    90\u2192* Teams can evolve schemas without cross-team migration battles.\n    91\u2192* Disaster recovery is narrowed to datastore-specific SLAs.\n    92\u2192\n    93\u2192Negative\n    94\u2192* Ops: multiple backup/restore, monitoring, and upgrade procedures.\n    95\u2192* Observability: needing distributed tracing across store boundaries.\n    96\u2192* Onboarding: developers must learn \u2265 3 query DSLs.\n    97\u2192\n    98\u2192Mitigations\n    99\u2192* Unified secrets via Vault; IaC modules standardize provisioning.\n   100\u2192* Cross-store dashboards in Grafana/Loki/Tempo.\n   101\u2192* Internal workshops and cheat-sheets for new engineers.\n   102\u2192\n   103\u2192## Related Decisions  \n   104\u2192* ADR-001 \u2013 Event-Driven Architecture  \n   105\u2192* ADR-002 \u2013 Domain-Driven Repository Pattern\n   106\u2192\n   107\u2192## Notes  \n   108\u2192This ADR will be revisited after the next academic year or when datastore OPEX exceeds 20 % of infrastructure budget.\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. 361\u2192  publish('session.expired', { userId: req.user?.id, reason: 'logout' }).catch(console.error);\n   362\u2192  return res.status(204).end();\n   363\u2192});\n   364\u2192\n   365\u2192export "     1\u2192```markdown\n     2\u2192# \ud83d\udcda PulseLearn Campus Hub \u2013 Course Service\n     3\u2192\n     4\u2192The **Course Service** is a stateless, event-driven micro-service that owns the **Course** aggregate in the PulseLearn ecosystem.  \n     5\u2192Its responsibilities include:\n     6\u2192\n     7\u2192* CRUD life-cycle of courses, modules, and lessons\n     8\u2192* Cohort enrolment & role management (student / instructor / TA)\n     9\u2192* Publishing domain events (`CourseCreated`, `ModuleUpdated`, `EnrollmentRevoked`, \u2026)\n    10\u2192* Consuming cross-cutting events (e.g., `UserDeleted`, `PaymentCaptured`)\n    11\u2192* Exposing a REST/JSON API for the web/mobile front-ends\n    12\u2192* Persisting data in PostgreSQL via Prisma ORM\n    13\u2192* Emitting real-time WebSocket updates to subscribed clients (via the Gateway)\n    14\u2192\n    15\u2192> TL;DR \u2014 **The Course Service is the single source of truth for all course metadata in PulseLearn.**\n    16\u2192\n    17\u2192\n    18\u2192---\n    19\u2192\n    20\u2192## \u2728 Quick Start\n    21\u2192\n    22\u2192```bash\n    23\u2192# 1. 94\u2192| GET    | `/` | List courses (paginated) | Optional |\n    95\u2192| GET    | `/:courseId` | Get single course | Optional |\n    96\u2192| POST   | `/` | Create new course | Instructor |\n    97\u2192| PATCH  | `/:courseId` | Update course | Instructor (owner) |\n    98\u2192| DELETE | `/:courseId` | Soft-delete course | Admin / Instructor |\n    99\u2192| POST   | `/:courseId/enroll` | Enroll user | Authenticated |\n   100\u2192| DELETE | `/:courseId/enroll/:userId` | Remove enrollment | Instructor / Admin |\n   101\u2192\n   102\u2192Full OpenAPI 3 schema lives under `src/api/openapi.yaml` and is served at `/docs` (Swagger UI).\n   103\u2192\n   104\u2192---\n   105\u2192\n   106\u2192## \ud83d\uddc4\ufe0f Data Model (Prisma)\n   107\u2192\n   108\u2192```prisma\n   109\u2192model Course {\n   110\u2192  id          String    @id @default(cuid())\n   111\u2192  title       String\n   112\u2192  description String\n   113\u2192  thumbnail   String?    @db.VarChar(2048)\n   114\u2192  visibility  Visibility @default(PUBLIC)\n   115\u2192  modules     Module[]\n   116\u2192  ownerId     String\n   117\u2192  owner       User       @relation(fields: [ownerId], references: [id])\n   118\u2192  enrollments Enrollment[]\n   119\u2192  createdAt   DateTime   @default(now())\n   120\u2192  updatedAt   DateTime   @updatedAt\n   121\u2192}\n   122\u2192```\n   123\u2192\n   124\u2192See `schema.prisma` for the full ERD.\n   125\u2192\n   126\u2192---\n   127\u2192\n   128\u2192## \ud83d\udce3 Domain Events\n   129\u2192\n   130\u2192| Event 186\u2192\n   187\u21921. **Unit Tests** \u2013 Pure functions, domain logic \u2013 run in CI on every PR.  \n   188\u21922. **Integration Tests** \u2013 Spawns an ephemeral Postgres DB (via `docker-compose -p test`).  \n   189\u21923. **Contract Tests** \u2013 Pact JS ensures consumers (front-end) respect the OpenAPI spec.  \n   190\u2192\n   191\u2192Run all locally:\n   192\u2192\n Prometheus metrics exposed on `/metrics`  \n   205\u2192\n   206\u2192K8s readiness/liveness probes hit `/healthz` and `/readyz`.  \n   207\u2192\n   208\u2192---\n   209\u2192\n   210\u2192## \u26a0\ufe0f Gotchas\n   211\u2192\n   212\u2192* Publishing events before DB commit may lead to lost messages. We use the **Transactional Outbox** pattern to guarantee atomicity.\n   213\u2192* Large cohort imports should be processed via the **Bulk Enroll** endpoint (`/api/v1/courses/:id/enroll/bulk`) which streams CSV rows.\n   214\u2192* **Idempotency-Key** header is required on all mutating requests to avoid duplicate transactions.\n   215\u2192\n   216\u2192---\n   217\u2192\n   218\u2192## \ud83e\udd1d Contributing\n   219\u2192\n   220\u21921. \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n  const handleReady = () => {\n    setReady(true);\n    /* Seek to previous checkpoint (if any) */\n    if (!isNearlyEqual(startAt, 0)) {\n      playerRef.current?.seekTo(startAt, 'seconds');\n 'LectureResumed' : 'LecturePaused', {\n        at: roundTime(progress.playedSeconds),\n      });\n      return next;\n    });\n  };\n\n  const handleVolume = () => setMuted((m) => !m);\n\n  const  const toggleFullscreen = () => {\n    if (screenfull.isEnabled && containerRef.current) {\n      screenfull.toggle(containerRef.current);\n    }\n  };\n\n  useEffect(() => {\n    if (!screenfull.isEnabled) return;\n\n    const onChange = () => setIsFullscreen(screenfull.isFullscreen);\n    screenfull.on('change', onChange);\n    return () => screenfull.off('change', onChange);\n \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n ws.addEventListener('open', () => {\n        setLoading(false);\n        setError(null);\n        // Reset reconnect back-off on successful connection\n        reconnectIntervalRef.current = INITIAL_RECONNECT_INTERVAL;\n      });\n\n      ws.addEventListener('message', (msg) => {\n        try {\n          const json = JSON.parse(msg.data);\n\n          /**\n           * Backend sends const existing = acc.find((d) => d.course === curr.course);\n              if (!existing || existing.percent < curr.percent) {\n                return [...acc.filter((d) => d.course !== curr.course), reconnectIntervalRef.current * 2,\n          MAX_RECONNECT_INTERVAL,\n        );\n\n        setTimeout(connect, timeout);\n      });\n\n      ws.addEventListener('error', (e) => {\n        // We close We rely on NATS Streaming (Stan) for at-least-once\n * delivery semantics and use pino for structured logging.\n *\n * This module exposes a singleton instance that is:\n *  \u2013 lazily connected (first call to `publish`)\n *  \u2013 resilient (auto-reconnects with back-off and drains on shutdown)\n *  \u2013 schema-aware (basic validation and version stamping)\n *\n * Environment variables:\n *  NATS_CLUSTER_ID  \u2013 cluster identifier configured on the NATS server\n *  NATS_CLIENT_ID   \u2013 unique client id for this producer\n *  NATS_URL         \u2013 tunneling URL (e.g. nats://user:pass@localhost:4222)\n */\n\n'use strict';\n\nconst stan    = require('node-nats-streaming');\nconst { v4: uuid } = require('uuid');\nconst pino    = require('pino');\n\n// ---- Configuration ---------------------------------------------------------\n\nconst {\n  NATS_CLUSTER_ID = 'pulselrn',\n  NATS_CLIENT_ID  = `course-svc-producer-${uuid().substring(0, 8)}`,\n  NATS_URL        = 'nats://localhost:4222',\n  NODE_ENV        = 'development'\n} = process.env;\n\nconst LOGGER = pino({\n  level : NODE_ENV === 'production' ? 'info' : 'debug',\n  name  : 'course-service:event-producer'\n});\n\n// Publish-side subject naming convention\nconst SUBJECTS = {\n  COURSE_CREATED : 'course.created',\n  COURSE_UPDATED : 'course.updated',\n  COURSE_ARCHIVED: 'course.archived'\n};\n\n// Maximum time in milliseconds the client will wait for an ACK from NATS\nconst ACK_WAIT_MILLIS = 5_000;\n\n// ---- Internal Helpers ------------------------------------------------------\n\n/**\n * Serialise payload and enrich with envelope metadata.\n * @param {String} eventType\n * @param {Object} data\n */\nfunction buildMessage(eventType, data) {\n  return JSON.stringify({\n    id         : uuid(),       // event identifier for idempotency\n    version    : 1,            // domain event schema version\n    timestamp  : new Date().toISOString(),\n    emitter    : 'course-service',\n    event      : eventType,\n    payload    : data\n  });\n}\n\n/**\n * Simple schema guard for course payloads.\n * In production we could delegate to a proper JSON-schema validator\n * such as Ajv; here we add a minimal safeguard so we do not publish\n * garbage messages onto the bus.\n */\nfunction validateCoursePayload(payload = {}) {\n  if (!payload.id || typeof payload.id !== 'string') {\n    throw new Error('Invalid payload: \"id\" is required and must be a string');\n  }\n  if (!payload.title || typeof payload.title !== 'string') {\n    throw new Error('Invalid payload: \"title\" is required and must be a string');\n  }\n}\n\n// ---- Producer Implementation ----------------------------------------------\n\nclass EventProducer {\n\n  constructor() {\n    this._stan   = null;\n    this._ready  = false;\n    this._queue  = [];\n    this._drainInProgress = false;\n  }\n\n  /**\n   * Lazily create a connection to the NATS Streaming cluster.\n   * Connection is initialised only once per process.\n   * @returns {Promise<void>}\n   */\n  async _connect() {\n    if (this._stan || this._ready) return;\n    LOGGER.info({ cluster: NATS_CLUSTER_ID, client: NATS_CLIENT_ID, url: NATS_URL },\n                'Connecting to NATS Streaming\u2026');\n\n    this._stan = stan.connect(NATS_CLUSTER_ID, NATS_CLIENT_ID, { url: NATS_URL });\n\n    // Promisify connection lifecycle\n    await new Promise((resolve, reject) => {\n      const onConnect = () => {\n        this._ready = true;\n        LOGGER.info('NATS Streaming connection established \u2705');\n        this._flushQueue(); // emit messages that were queued before ready\n        resolve();\n      };\n\n      const onError = (err) => {\n        LOGGER.error({ err }, 'Unable to connect to NATS Streaming \u274c');\n        reject(err);\n      };\n\n      this._stan.once('connect', onConnect);\n      this._stan.once('error',   onError);\n    });\n\n    // Attach common listeners AFTER the initial promise resolution\n    this._stan.on('close',  () => LOGGER.warn('NATS connection closed'));\n    this._stan.on('reconnect', () => LOGGER.info('NATS reconnected'));\n    this._stan.on('disconnect', () => LOGGER.warn('NATS disconnected'));\n  }\n\n  /**\n   * Drain NATS connection gracefully before process exit.\n   */\n  async close() {\n    if (!this._stan || this._drainInProgress) return;\n    this._drainInProgress = true;\n\n    LOGGER.info('Draining NATS Streaming connection before shutdown\u2026');\n    await new Promise((resolve) => {\n      this._stan.drain(() => {\n        LOGGER.info('NATS drain complete, closing connection');\n        this._stan.close();\n        resolve();\n      });\n    });\n  }\n\n  /**\n   * Publish raw subject + message\n   * @param {String} subject\n   * @param {String} message   \u2013 already JSON serialised\n   * @param {Object} options   \u2013 optional metadata (e.g. persistentName)\n   * @returns {Promise<void>}\n   */\n  async _publish(subject, message, options = {}) {\n    await this._connect();\n\n    return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {\n      const guid = this._stan.publish(subject, message, (err, ackGuid) => {\n        if (err) {\n          LOGGER.error({ err, subject, guid }, 'Failed to publish message');\n          return reject(err);\n        }\n        LOGGER.debug({ subject, guid: ackGuid }, 'Event published');\n        resolve();\n      });\n\n      // Fallback: if no ack within ACK_WAIT_MILLIS, reject\n      setTimeout(() => {\n        reject(new Error(`ACK timeout after ${ACK_WAIT_MILLIS}ms for guid: ${guid}`));\n      }, ACK_WAIT_MILLIS).unref();\n    });\n  }\n\n  /**\n   * Queue messages if connection hasn't been established yet.\n   * This prevents any writes being lost during cold starts.\n   */\n  _queueMessage(subject, message) {\n    this._queue.push({ subject, message });\n  }\n\n  _flushQueue() {\n    if (!this._queue.length || !this._ready) return;\n\n    LOGGER.info(`Flushing ${this._queue.length} queued event(s)`);\n    this._queue.forEach(({ subject, message }) => {\n      this._stan.publish(subject, message, (err) => {\n        if (err) {\n          LOGGER.error({ subject, err }, 'Failed to publish queued event');\n        }\n      });\n    });\n    this._queue.length = 0;\n  }\n\n  // ---------------------------------------------------\n  // Domain-specific API\n  // ---------------------------------------------------\n\n  /**\n   * Course Created domain event publisher.\n   * @param {Object} course \u2013 plain JS object { id, title, \u2026 }\n   */\n  async courseCreated(course) {\n    try {\n      validateCoursePayload(course);\n      const msg = buildMessage('CourseCreated', course);\n      await this._publish(SUBJECTS.COURSE_CREATED, msg);\n    } catch (err) {\n      LOGGER.error({ err, course }, 'Unable to publish CourseCreated event');\n      throw err;\n    }\n  }\n\n  /**\n   * Course Updated domain event publisher.\n   * @param {Object} course \u2013 plain JS object { id, title, \u2026 }\n   */\n  async courseUpdated(course) {\n    try {\n      validateCoursePayload(course);\n      const msg = buildMessage('CourseUpdated', course);\n      await this._publish(SUBJECTS.COURSE_UPDATED, msg);\n    } catch (err) {\n      LOGGER.error({ err, course }, 'Unable to publish CourseUpdated event');\n      throw err;\n    }\n  }\n\n  /**\n   * Course archived event publisher.\n   * @param {Object} course \u2013 minimal object { id, archivedAt }\n   */\n  async courseArchived(course) {\n    if (!course.id) {\n      throw new Error('Invalid payload: \"id\" is required for archive event');\n    }\n\n    const msg = buildMessage('CourseArchived', course);\n    try {\n      await this._publish(SUBJECTS.COURSE_ARCHIVED, msg);\n    } catch (err) {\n      LOGGER.error({ err, course }, 'Unable to publish CourseArchived event');\n      throw err;\n    }\n  }\n}\n\n// ---- Singleton Export ------------------------------------------------------\n\nconst producerInstance = new EventProducer();\n\n// Clean up before the Node process is terminated\n['SIGINT', 'SIGTERM', 'SIGQUIT'].forEach((signal) => {\n  process.on(signal, async () => {\n    LOGGER.info({ signal }, 'Received termination signal');\n    await producerInstance.close();\n    process.exit(0);\n  });\n});\n\nmodule.exports = producerInstance;\n```",

const where = { id };\n    if (typeof expectedVersion === 'number') {\n      where.version = expectedVersion;\n    }\n\n    const [affected, rows] = await this.Course.update(updates, {\n      where,\n Context \u2011 Why change?\n\nPulseLearn Campus Hub (PCH) is experiencing rapid feature growth:\n\n* Real-time dashboards for quiz progress, peer-review feedback, and badge awards  \n* A new gamification engine that recalculates points on every learning event  \n* Audit-ready reporting for compliance and accreditation bodies  \n\nThe existing CRUD-centric model has hit several limits:\n\n| Pain-Point                          | Symptom                                                                             |\n|------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| Data-coupling                       | Multiple bounded contexts write to the same tables, causing noisy merge conflicts. |\n| Missed notifications                | Lost WebSocket messages because they were dispatched directly from HTTP handlers.   |\n| Operational complexity              | Replaying history (e.g., to debug ranking errors) requires fragile SQL scripts.     |\n| Lack of temporal data               | Hard to answer \u201cWhat was Alice\u2019s score at 14:01 yesterday?\u201d                         |\n\nTo address these, we want:\n\n1. **Immutable event log** \u2013 the single source of truth  \n2. **Replayability** \u2013 rebuild read-models at any point in time  \n3. **Loose coupling** \u2013 services subscribe to what they need, when they need it  \n4. **Scalability** \u2013 horizontal partitioning of event streams  \n\nApache **Kafka** is already used in our data-analytics pipeline; adopting it as the system event backbone is a natural next step.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Decision\n\nWe will adopt **event sourcing** for all new domain workflows and gradually migrate existing ones.  \nKafka will act as the **persistent event store** (commit log) and **message bus**.  \nSpecifics:\n\n1. **Each bounded context owns its topic(s)** \u2013 e.g. `education.assignment`, `identity.session`, `gamification.badge`.\n2. **Events are immutable** JSON messages, versioned via a `schemaVersion` field; schema registry enforced at the gateway.\n3. **Append-only**: write operations emit events; read models are derived via consumer projections.\n4. **Exactly-once** semantics: achieved by Kafka idempotent producers + transactional writes to outbox tables when necessary.\n5. **Snapshot strategy**: Long-lived aggregates publish `*.snapshot` events every *n* revisions to shorten replay time.\n6. **Backward compatibility**: Services must ignore unknown fields and can only add optional fields to existing event versions.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Consequences\n\nPositive:\n\n* **Auditability** \u2013 every state change is traceable.  \n* **Resilience** \u2013 consumers can restart and replay without data loss.  \n* **Scalable read models** \u2013 each service builds its own query-optimized projection.  \n\nNegative / Trade-offs:\n\n* **Write complexity** \u2013 commands must succeed or be compensated by new events.  \n* **Learning curve** \u2013 developers must understand eventual consistency.  \n* **Storage cost** \u2013 Kafka cluster size grows with retained history.  \n\n---\n\n## 4. Implementation Sketch (JavaScript / Node.js)\n\nBelow are cut-down excerpts from production code to guide contributors.  \nAll examples assume Node.js \u2265 18, TypeScript, and the `kafkajs` client.\n\n### 4.1 Common Infrastructure\n\n```ts\n// src/infrastructure/kafka/kafkaClient.ts\nimport { Kafka, logLevel } from 'kafkajs';\nimport config from '../../config';\n\nexport const kafka = new Kafka({\n  clientId: 'pulselearn-campus-hub',\n  brokers : config.kafka.brokers,\n  ssl     : true,\n  sasl    : {\n    mechanism : 'scram-sha-256',\n    username  : config.kafka.username,\n    password  : config.kafka.password,\n  },\n  logLevel: logLevel.WARN,\n});\n\nexport function topicName(boundedContext: string, suffix = ''): string {\n  return `${config.env}.${boundedContext}${suffix && `.${suffix}`}`;\n}\n```\n\n### 4.2 Event Contracts\n\n```ts\n// src/domain/events/AssignmentSubmittedEvent.ts\nimport { z } from 'zod';\n\nexport const AssignmentSubmittedEventSchema = z.object({\n  schemaVersion  : z.literal(1),\n  eventId        : z.string().uuid(),\n  aggregateId    : z.string().uuid(),   // Assignment ID\n  type           : z.literal('AssignmentSubmitted'),\n  occurredAt     : z.string().datetime({ offset: true }),\n  payload        : z.object({\n    courseId  : z.string().uuid(),\n    studentId : z.string().uuid(),\n    fileUrl   : z.string().url(),\n  }),\n});\n\nexport type AssignmentSubmittedEvent = z.infer<typeof AssignmentSubmittedEventSchema>;\n```\n\n### 4.3 Producer (Command Handler -> Event)\n\n```ts\n// src/application/commands/submitAssignment.ts\nimport { AssignmentSubmittedEvent } from '../../domain/events/AssignmentSubmittedEvent';\nimport { kafka, topicName } from '../../infrastructure/kafka/kafkaClient';\nimport { randomUUID } from 'crypto';\n\nexport async function submitAssignment(cmd: {\n  courseId: string;\n  studentId: string;\n  fileUrl: string;\n}): Promise<void> {\n  // Business validation omitted for brevity\n\n  const event: AssignmentSubmittedEvent = {\n    schemaVersion : 1,\n    eventId       : randomUUID(),\n    aggregateId   : randomUUID(),\n    type          : 'AssignmentSubmitted',\n    occurredAt    : new Date().toISOString(),\n    payload       : cmd,\n  };\n\n  const producer = kafka.producer({ idempotent: true });\n  await producer.connect();\n\n  try {\n    await producer.send({\n      topic: topicName('education.assignment'),\n      messages: [\n        {\n          key  : event.aggregateId,\n          value: JSON.stringify(event),\n          headers: {\n            'schema-version': '1',\n            'event-type'    : event.type,\n          },\n        },\n      ],\n    });\n  } finally {\n    await producer.disconnect();\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### 4.4 Consumer Projection (Gamification Points)\n\n```ts\n// src/projections/gamification/pointsProjector.ts\nimport { kafka, topicName } from '../../infrastructure/kafka/kafkaClient';\nimport { AssignmentSubmittedEventSchema } from '../../domain/events/AssignmentSubmittedEvent';\nimport pointsRepo from '../../repositories/pointsRepository';\n\nexport async function runPointsProjector(): Promise<void> {\n  const consumer = kafka.consumer({\n    groupId: 'gamification-points-projector-v1',\n  });\n\n  await consumer.connect();\n  await consumer.subscribe({\n    topic: topicName('education.assignment'),\n    fromBeginning: false,\n  });\n\n  await consumer.run({\n    eachMessage: async ({ message, partition }) => {\n      try {\n        const raw = message.value?.toString() ?? '{}';\n        const parsed = AssignmentSubmittedEventSchema.parse(JSON.parse(raw));\n\n        await pointsRepo.increment(\n          parsed.payload.studentId,\n          /* points = */ 5,\n        );\n\n        console.info(\n          `[PointProjector] +5 for student=${parsed.payload.studentId} (partition=${partition})`,\n        );\n      } catch (err) {\n        // DLQ or retry logic could be implemented here\n        console.error('[PointProjector] Failed to process message', err);\n      }\n    },\n  });\n}\n```\n\n### 4.5 Snapshotter Utility\n\n```ts\n// src/utils/snapshotter.ts\nimport { kafka, topicName } from '../infrastructure/kafka/kafkaClient';\n\nexport async function publishSnapshot<T>({\n  boundedContext,\n  aggregateName,\n  aggregateId,\n  revision,\n  state,\n}: {\n  boundedContext: string;\n  aggregateName: string;\n  aggregateId: string;\n  revision: number;\n  state: T;\n}): Promise<void> {\n  const producer = kafka.producer();\n\n  await producer.connect();\n  try {\n    await producer.send({\n      topic: topicName(`${boundedContext}.${aggregateName}.snapshot`),\n      messages: [\n        {\n          key  : aggregateId,\n          value: JSON.stringify({\n            schemaVersion: 1,\n            type         : `${aggregateName}.snapshot`,\n            revision,\n            occurredAt   : new Date().toISOString(),\n            state,\n          }),\n        },\n      ],\n    });\n  } finally {\n    await producer.disconnect();\n  }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Migration Path\n\n1. **Brown-field integration**: legacy CRUD modules will emit events in a \u201cchange-data-capture\u201d style, then slowly migrate command handling logic.  \n2. **Feature toggles**: Read models behind `/v2/` API routes will use event projections; `/v1/` remains on relational reads.  \n3. **Runbook & SRE**: New runbooks added for Kafka cluster monitoring (Lag, ISR, Disk usage).  \n4. **Developer enablement**: Internal workshop + \u201cEvent Sourcing 101\u201d wiki page.  \n\n---\n\n## 6. Rejected Alternatives\n\n* **RabbitMQ + Outbox pattern** \u2013 flexible routing but lacks strong log-compaction and replay features.  \n* **Full CQRS without Event Sourcing** \u2013 improves reads but doesn\u2019t solve auditability or temporal requirements.  \n\n---\n\n## 7. Open Issues / Next Steps\n\n1. Define retention policy per topic (regulatory requirement: 5-year minimum).  \n2. Agree on company-wide naming convention for events (`<Domain>.<Action><PastTense>`).  \n3. Evaluate Confluent Schema Registry vs. open-source alternatives.  \n4. Prototype snapshotting performance with 1M-event aggregate.  \n\n---\n\n> \u201cIf you treat data as immutable facts, your systems become a chronicle of truth, not just a reflection of the present.\u201d \u2013  Tech Lead, PCH\n```",
