    "content": "```markdown\n# ADR 001 \u2013 Adopt a Polyglot, Event-Driven Microservices Architecture\n\n* Status: **Accepted**  \n* Date: 2024-05-19  \n* Deciders: Architecture Council (CTO, Lead Backend, Lead Frontend, DevOps)  \n* Supersedes: N/A  \n* See also: 002-database-strategy.md, 003-auth-identity.md\n\n---\n\n## 1. Context  \n\nPulseLearn Campus Hub (PL-CH) must enable:\n\n1. Real-time, bidirectional interactions between thousands of concurrent users (students, teachers, admins).  \n2. Rapid feature evolution by autonomous domain-centric teams.  \n3. Fault-tolerance and graceful degradation of non-critical functionality (e.g., delayed \u201cBadgeAwarded\u201d events must **not** block quiz submissions).  \n4. Polyglot technology choices while enforcing a consistent ops/observability contract.  \n5. Compliance with FERPA, GDPR, and internal audit requirements such as end-to-end traceability and PII redaction policies.\n\nThe alternatives considered were:\n\n| Candidate                     | Pros                                                                                                    | Cons                                                                                                   |\n| ----------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n| A) Single-service (monolith)  | Simple to deploy, transactional consistency, easier local dev                                           | Scalability bottlenecks, slower team velocity, long-lived branches, risky deployments                  |\n| B) Self-contained services    | Autonomy per bounded context, independent UI + API bundles                                              | Risk of UI duplication, heavier front-end orchestration                                                |\n| **C) Microservices + Event Bus** | Loose coupling via events, horizontal scalability, team autonomy, tech polyglot, easier domain modeling | Requires distributed tracing, eventual consistency semantics, operational complexity                   |\n| D) Serverless (FaaS only)     | Zero infra management, cost per execution                                                               | Cold starts, vendor lock-in, limited long-running connections, complex local testing                   |\n\nAfter evaluating traffic patterns, compliance constraints, and organisation structure (5 cross-functional squads), option **C** was chosen.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Decision  \n\nWe will build **PulseLearn Campus Hub** as an **event-driven microservices system**:\n\n1. **Domain-Oriented Microservices**  \n   \u2022 Each service owns a bounded context & data store (e.g., `UserProfile`, `LearningPath`, `Achievement`, `Notification`).  \n   \u2022 Services communicate asynchronously via a Kafka compatible bus (NATS JetStream in staging, Confluent Cloud in prod).  \n   \u2022 REST/gRPC APIs remain for synchronous \u201cquery\u201d use-cases and external integrations (admin panel, LTI).  \n\n2. **Event Taxonomy**  \n   \u2022 All domain events adopt the CloudEvents 1.0 spec.  \n   \u2022 Topic naming: `pl.<boundedContext>.<eventName>.<version>` (e.g., `pl.achievement.badge_awarded.v1`).  \n   \u2022 Payloads are validated with versioned Avro schemas stored in Schema Registry.  \n\n3. **Shared Platform Libraries**  \n   \u2022 We ship an OSS-friendly **`@pl/platform`** JavaScript package that wraps NATS/Kafka producers & consumers, tracing, and idempotency utilities (see snippet below).  \n   \u2022 Analogous libraries will exist for Python, Go, and Java to keep polyglot parity.  \n\n4. **Observability & Resilience**  \n   \u2022 OpenTelemetry for distributed tracing, correlated logs, metrics (`traceId` + `spanId` pass via W3C `traceparent`).  \n   \u2022 Circuit breakers (opossum) guard cross-service HTTP calls.  \n   \u2022 Retry, DLQ, and \u201cparking lot\u201d patterns for poison messages.  \n\n5. **Security**  \n   \u2022 mTLS between services (Linkerd service mesh).  \n   \u2022 SPIFFE IDs for zero-trust identity.  \n   \u2022 PII encrypted at rest (PostgreSQL + envelope encryption).  \n\n---\n\n## 3. Consequences  \n\nPositive:  \n\u2713 Independent deployability enables <15 min release cadence per squad.  \n\u2713 Horizontal scaling by workload (e.g., `RecommendationService` auto-scales via KEDA based on Kafka lag).  \n\u2713 Failure isolation\u2014`SearchIndexer` crash has no direct impact on \u201cQuizCompletion\u201d UX.  \n\nNegative:  \n\u2717 Added operational overhead: CI/CD pipelines, playbooks, Terraform modules per service.  \n\u2717 Data consistency becomes eventual; we must adopt Saga patterns for workflows like \u201cPurchaseCourse \u2192 ActivateAccess \u2192 EmitInvoice\u201d.  \n\u2717 On-call complexity: PagerDuty rotations per squad, plus a shared SRE roster for platform components (Kafka, Linkerd, Istio ingress).\n\n---\n\n## 4. Implementation Sketch  \n\n### Mermaid: High-level view\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart LR\n    subgraph Frontend\n        ReactApp[Web SPA]\n        MobileApp[React Native]\n    end\n    ReactApp -->|REST: /api/v1| APIGateway\n    MobileApp -->|GraphQL| APIGateway\n    APIGateway --> AuthSvc[(Auth Service)]\n    APIGateway --> UserSvc[(User Profile)]\n    APIGateway --> CourseSvc[(Course Catalog)]\n    style APIGateway fill:#f5f5f5,stroke:#333,stroke-width:1px\n    \n    %% Event Bus\n    subgraph EventBus[\"NATS / Kafka\"]\n        NATS[(JetStream Topic)]\n    end\n    \n    CourseSvc -->|pl.course.uploaded| NATS\n    UserSvc -->|pl.user.session_expired| NATS\n    NATS --> SearchSvc[(Search Indexer)]\n    NATS --> BadgeSvc[(Achievement)]\n    NATS --> RecSvc[(Recommendation)]\n```\n\n### Shared JS Event Library (`@pl/platform`)\n\n```javascript\n// @pl/platform/lib/event-bus.js\nimport { connect, StringCodec } from 'nats';\nimport { v4 as uuid } from 'uuid';\nimport * as otel from '@opentelemetry/api';\n\n/**\n * EventBus singleton to publish/subscribe CloudEvents-compliant messages.\n */\nexport class EventBus {\n  static instance;\n\n  /**\n   * Initialise a NATS connection (lazy).\n   * @param {object} config - {servers: string, jwt?: string, nkey?: string}\n   */\n  static async init(config) {\n    if (!EventBus.instance) {\n      EventBus.instance = new EventBus(config);\n      await EventBus.instance._connect();\n    }\n    return EventBus.instance;\n  }\n\n  constructor(config) {\n    this.config = config;\n    this.sc = StringCodec();\n  }\n\n  async _connect() {\n    try {\n      this.nc = await connect(this.config);\n      this.js = this.nc.jetstream();\n      console.info('[EventBus] Connected to NATS');\n    } catch (err) {\n      console.error('[EventBus] Connection error', err);\n      throw err;\n    }\n  }\n\n  /**\n   * Publish a CloudEvent to the given topic.\n   * @param {string} topic - e.g. \"pl.achievement.badge_awarded.v1\"\n   * @param {object} data - event payload\n   * @param {object} [options] - headers, trace context, etc.\n   */\n  async publish(topic, data, options = {}) {\n    if (!this.nc) throw new Error('EventBus not initialised');\n    const span = otel.trace.getTracer('pl-platform').startSpan(`publish:${topic}`);\n    try {\n      const event = {\n        id: uuid(),\n        source: 'pulselearn-campus-hub',\n        specversion: '1.0',\n        type: topic,\n        time: new Date().toISOString(),\n        datacontenttype: 'application/json',\n        data,\n      };\n      // propagate trace context\n      const headers = this._buildHeaders(span, options.headers);\n      await this.js.publish(topic, this.sc.encode(JSON.stringify(event)), { headers });\n      span.setStatus({ code: otel.SpanStatusCode.OK });\n    } catch (err) {\n      span.setStatus({ code: otel.SpanStatusCode.ERROR, message: err.message });\n      throw err;\n    } finally {\n      span.end();\n    }\n  }\n\n  /**\n   * Subscribe to a topic with durable consumer semantics.\n   * @param {string} topic\n   * @param {string} durableName\n   * @param {(evt: object) => Promise<void>} handler\n   */\n  async subscribe(topic, durableName, handler) {\n    const subOpts = { durable: durableName, manualAck: true, ackWait: 60_000 };\n    const sub = await this.js.subscribe(topic, subOpts);\n    console.info(`[EventBus] Subscribed to ${topic}`);\n\n    (async () => {\n      for await (const m of sub) {\n        const span = otel.trace.getTracer('pl-platform').startSpan(`consume:${topic}`);\n        try {\n          const evt = JSON.parse(this.sc.decode(m.data));\n          await handler(evt);\n          m.ack();\n          span.setStatus({ code: otel.SpanStatusCode.OK });\n        } catch (err) {\n          console.error('[EventBus] Handler error', err);\n          // let JetStream redeliver, or add to DLQ via a header\n          span.setStatus({ code: otel.SpanStatusCode.ERROR, message: err.message });\n        } finally {\n          span.end();\n        }\n      }\n    })().catch((err) => console.error('[EventBus] Async iteration error', err));\n  }\n\n  _buildHeaders(span, extra = {}) {\n    const headers = this.nc.headers();\n    const ctx = otel.trace.setSpan(otel.context.active(), span);\n    otel.propagation.inject(ctx, headers, {\n      set: (carrier, key, value) => carrier.set(key, value),\n    });\n    Object.entries(extra).forEach(([k, v]) => headers.set(k, v));\n    return headers;\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Saga Orchestration Example (Enroll Premium Course)\n\n```javascript\n// services/payment/src/enrollCourseSaga.js\nimport { EventBus } from '@pl/platform';\nimport { db } from '../db';\nimport { generateInvoice } from '../billing';\nimport { logger } from '../logger';\n\nexport async function registerEventHandlers() {\n  const bus = await EventBus.init({ servers: process.env.NATS_URL });\n\n  // listen to PaymentCaptured\n  await bus.subscribe('pl.payment.captured.v1', 'enroll-premium-course', async (evt) => {\n    const { userId, courseId, paymentId } = evt.data;\n    logger.info('Payment captured', { userId, courseId, paymentId });\n\n    // Step 1: Activate access in course service (synchronous call)\n    try {\n      await activateCourseAccess(userId, courseId);\n    } catch (err) {\n      logger.error('Course activation failed', err);\n      // emit compensating event\n      await bus.publish('pl.payment.refund_requested.v1', { paymentId, reason: 'COURSE_ACTIVATION_FAILED' });\n      return;\n    }\n\n    // Step 2: Emit EnrollmentGranted event\n    await bus.publish('pl.enrollment.granted.v1', { userId, courseId });\n\n    // Step 3: Issue invoice (local DB + external PDF generator)\n    try {\n      const invoiceId = await generateInvoice({ userId, paymentId });\n      await db.invoice.markSent(invoiceId);\n    } catch (err) {\n      logger.error('Invoice generation failed', err);\n      // Non-blocking; instructor & finance will be alerted via DLQ consumer\n    }\n  });\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Alternatives Explored (But NOT Chosen)\n\n* **Monolith + Event Module** \u2013 insufficient isolation; high coordination cost for multi-squad development.  \n* **Pure Serverless** \u2013 latency and unpredictable cost for high-frequency message streams (quizzes, edits).  \n* **gRPC-only Service Mesh** \u2013 synchronous coupling failed chaos testing when `AnalyticsService` induced 40 % error rate.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Validation & Next Steps\n\n1. Platform Team to spin up NATS + JetStream in staging (k8s operator).  \n2. Each squad migrates at least one bounded context to the new pattern by Sprint 14.  \n3. Evaluate Confluent vs Redpanda for prod by Q3.  \n4. Conduct load test: 50k concurrent websocket sessions, publish 2k events/s, < 200 ms P99 end-to-end latency.  \n\n---\n\n## 7. ----------------------------------\n * \u2022 Configuration needs to adapt to dynamic container / k8s deployments.\n * \u2022 Runtime values (hostnames, ports, ssl paths) come from ENV vars.\n * \u2022 We want validation, helpful error messages and unit-testability.\n *\n * Usage\n * -----\n *  $ node nginx.conf [output-path]\n *\n *  \u2013 If executed via `node`, the generated configuration is written to\n *    the provided output path (default: /etc/nginx/conf.d/pulselearn.conf)\n *  \u2013 When imported (`require('./nginx.conf')`) the `buildNginxConfig`\n *    method returns the config as a string.\n */\n\n'use strict';\n\nconst fs   = require('fs');\nconst path = require('path');\nconst os   = Schema\n////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n\nconst ENV_SCHEMA = {\n  /** Comma-separated hosts for each micro-service.\n   *  Example: AUTH_SERVICE_HOSTS=\"auth1:4000,auth2:4000\" */\n  AUTH_SERVICE_HOSTS        : { required: true  },\n  USER_SERVICE_HOSTS        : { required: true  },\n  CONTENT_SERVICE_HOSTS     : { required: true  },\n  NOTIFICATION_SERVICE_HOSTS: { required: true  },\n\n  /** SSL certificate / key */\n  SSL_CERT_PATH             : { required: false, default: '/etc/ssl/certs/pulselearn.crt' },\n  SSL_KEY_PATH              : { required: false, default: '/etc/ssl/private/pulselearn.key' },\n\n  /** Optional toggles */\n  FORCE_SSL                 : { required: false, default: 'true' },\n  CLIENT_MAX_BODY_SIZE_MB   : { required: false, default: '20' },\n  RATE_LIMIT_REQ_PER_MIN    : { required: false, default: '600' },\n\n  /** Logging */\n  ACCESS_LOG_PATH           : { required: false, default: '/var/log/nginx/access.log' },\n  ERROR_LOG_PATH            : { required: false, default: '/var/log/nginx/error.log' }\n};\n\n/**\n * Load and validate environment variables against the schema.\n * Throws if a required variable is missing.\n */\nfunction loadEnv () {\n  const conf = {};\n\n  Object.entries(ENV_SCHEMA).forEach(([key, meta]) => {\n    const value = process.env[key] ?? meta.default;\n    if (meta.required && (value === undefined || value === null)) {\n      throw new Error(`Missing required environment variable: ${key}`);\n    }\n    conf[key] = value;\n  });\n\n .map(host => host.trim())\n    .filter(Boolean)\n    .map(host => `        server ${host};`)\n    .join('\\n');\n}\n\n/**\n * Render a single upstream block.\n *\n * @param {string} name       - Upstream name (e.g. \"auth_service\").\n * @param {string} hosts      - Comma-separated list of host:port targets.\n * @param {object} [opts={}]  - Options like keepalive settings.\n */\nfunction renderUpstream (name, hosts, opts = {}) {\n  const keepalive = opts.keepalive ?? 64;\n  return `\n    upstream ${name} {\n${toUpstreamServers(hosts)}\n        keepalive ${keepalive};\n ['content_service',       env.CONTENT_SERVICE_HOSTS],\n    ['notification_service',  env.NOTIFICATION_SERVICE_HOSTS]\n  ].map(([name, hosts]) => renderUpstream(name, hosts)).join('\\n');\n\n  const LOCATIONS =\n      renderLocation('/auth/',         'auth_service')          +\n      renderLocation('/users/',        'user_service')          +\n      renderLocation('/content/',      'content_service')       +\n      renderLocation('/notifications/','notification_service');\n\n  const SSL_CONFIG = (env.FORCE_SSL === 'true')\n    ? `\n        listen 443 ssl http2;\n   });\n *\n * All functions return native Promises and surface errors, allowing\n * consumers to decide how to handle failures within UI components.\n * -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n */\nconst STORAGE_KEY = {\n  ACCESS: 'pulselearn.access_token',\n  REFRESH: 'pulselearn.refresh_token',\n};\n\nconst eslint-enable no-param-reassign */\n    return config;\n  },\n  error => Promise.reject(error),\n);\n\n/**\n * Response interceptor\n *   \u2013 Handles 401s by attempting a refresh flow once per request.\n *   \u2013 Queues parallel requests while a refresh is in flight to avoid\n *     a stampede of refresh calls.\n */\nlet isRefreshing = false;\nlet subscribers = [];\n\nfunction onRrefreshed(newToken) {\n  subscribers.forEach(cb => cb(newToken));\n  subscribers = [];\n}\n\nfunction addSubscriber(callback) {\n  subscribers.push(callback);\n}\n\nhttp.interceptors.response.use(\n  response => response,\n  async error => {\n    const { config, response } = error;\n    const isAuthError = response?.status === 401;\n    const hasRefreshToken = !!tokens.refresh;\n    const originalRequest = config;\n\n    if (!isAuthError || !hasRefreshToken) {\n      // Either not a 401 or we have nothing to refresh with.\n      return Promise.reject(error);\n    }\n\n    if (originalRequest._retry) {\n      // We already retried once & it failed again \u2192 logout.\n      clearTokens();\n      return Promise.reject(error);\n    }\n    originalRequest._retry = true;\n\n    // If another refresh request is already happening, queue.\n    if (isRefreshing) {\n      return new Promise(resolve => {\n        addSubscriber(token => {\n          originalRequest.headers.Authorization = `Bearer ${token}`;\n          resolve(http(originalRequest));\n        });\n      });\n    }\n\n    // Kick off refresh flow\n    isRefreshing = true;\n    try {\n      const newAccess = await refreshToken();\n      onRrefreshed(newAccess);\n\n      // Re-issue the original request with new token\n      originalRequest.headers.Authorization = `Bearer ${newAccess}`;\n      return http(originalRequest);\n    } catch (refreshErr) {\n      // Refresh failed \u2192 hard logout\n      clearTokens();\n      return Promise.reject(refreshErr);\n    } finally {\n      isRefreshing = false;\n    }\n  },\n);\n\n/**\n * Auth service\n * -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n */\nasync function login({ email, password }) {\n  try {\n    const { data } = await http.post('/auth/login', { email, password });\n    const { accessToken: access, refreshToken: refresh } = data;\n\n    if (!access || !refresh) {\n      throw new Error('Invalid auth payload from server');\n    }\n\n    persistTokens({ access, refresh });\n    return data;\n  } catch (err) {\n    clearTokens();\n    throw err;\n  }\n}\n\nasync function logout() {\n  try {\n    await http.post('/auth/logout');\n  } finally {\n    clearTokens();\n  }\n}\n\nasync function refreshToken() {\n  const { refresh } = tokens;\n  if (!refresh) throw new Error('No refresh token available');\n\n  const { data } = await http.post('/auth/refresh', { refreshToken: refresh });\n  const { accessToken: access, refreshToken: nextRefresh } = data;\n\n  if (!access) throw new Error('Failed to refresh token');\n\n  persistTokens({ access, refresh: nextRefresh || refresh });\n  return access;\n}\n\n/**\n * HTTP verb helpers\n * -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n */\nfunction unwrap(promise) {\n  return promise.then(res => res.data);\n}\n\nfunction get(url, config) {\n  return unwrap(http.get(url, config));\n}\n\nfunction post(url, payload, config) {\n  return unwrap(http.post(url, payload, config));\n}\n\nfunction put(url, payload, config) {\n  return unwrap(http.put(url, payload, config));\n}\n\nfunction patch(url, payload, config) {\n  return unwrap(http.patch(url, payload, config));\n}\n\nfunction del(url, config) {\n  return unwrap(http.delete(url, config));\n}\n\n/**\n * Server-Sent Events helper\n * -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n * Because native EventSource cannot send custom headers, we pass the\n * JWT via query-param.  The backend should validate the token server-side.\n */\nfunction connectEventStream(topics = [], { onMessage, onError, onOpen } = {}) {\n  const params = new URLSearchParams();\n\n  if (topics.length) params.set('topics', topics.join(','));\n  if (tokens.access) params.set('access_token', tokens.access);\n\n  const streamUrl = `${API_BASE_URL}/events/stream?${params.toString()}`;\n  const source = new EventSource(streamUrl, { withCredentials: true });\n\n  if (onOpen) source.addEventListener('open', onOpen);\n  if (onError) source.addEventListener('error', onError);\n  if (onMessage) source.addEventListener('message', onMessage);\n\n  return source; // allow caller to .close()\n}\n\n/**\n * Exports\n * -----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n */\nconst api = {\n  // raw axios instance if finer control is needed\n  client: http,\n\n  // CRUD helpers\n  get,\n  post,\n  put,\n  patch,\n  delete: del,\n\n  // grouped services\n  auth: {\n    login,\n    logout,\n    refresh: refreshToken,\n    get tokens() {\n      return { ...tokens };\n    },\n  },\n\n  events: {\n    connect: connectEventStream,\n  },\n};\n\nexport default api;\n```",

    "content": "<!--\n  ADR 003: Polyglot Persistence\n  PulseLearn Campus Hub\n  Status: Accepted\n  Date: 2024-05-28\n-->\n\n# 003 \u2013 Polyglot Persistence  \n\n## Status  \nAccepted \u2013 The decision has been implemented in `v1.4.0`.\n\n## Context  \nPulseLearn Campus Hub is an event-driven system with a variety of read/write patterns:\n\n* Write-intensive, append-only domain events (\u22488 k eps peak)  \n* Read-heavy social timelines that must fan-out to thousands of users in < 150 ms  \n* Strongly-consistent, relational data for billing, LMS compliance, and audit logs  \n* Full-text search over course content and peer-review comments  \n* Graph-style traversals for cohort relationships and content recommendations\n\nA single storage engine cannot optimize for all these needs without unacceptable trade-offs in performance, cost, or developer productivity. We therefore evaluated several strategies:\n\n| Option | Pros | Cons |\n| ------ | ---- | ---- |\n| 1. Single SQL RDBMS (PostgreSQL) | ACID, mature tooling | Hot partitions, expensive scaling, poor search |\n| 2. Single document DB (MongoDB) | Flexible schema, good read scaling | Event ordering issues, multi-doc transactions slower |\n| 3. Polyglot persistence *(selected)* | Fit-for-purpose stores, cost-effective | Operational complexity, cross-store transactions |\n\n## Decision  \nWe adopt **polyglot persistence**: each bounded context chooses the persistence technology that best serves its needs, within guardrails enforced by the Platform Team.\n\n1. **Event Store**  \n   *Technology:* Apache Kafka (log), TimescaleDB (cold storage)  \n   *Rationale:* Immutability, temporal queries, built-in replication.\n\n2. **User & Billing**  \n   *Technology:* PostgreSQL 15 with logical replication  \n   *Rationale:* Strong consistency for payments, GDPR data-subject requests.\n\n3. **Realtime Timelines & Notifications**  \n   *Technology:* Redis Cluster + Redis Streams  \n   *Rationale:* Sub-millisecond fan-out, pub/sub semantics, TTL-based eviction.\n\n4. **Search & Analytics**  \n   *Technology:* OpenSearch 2.x  \n   *Rationale:* Relevance scoring, aggregations, horizontal scaling.\n\n5. **Graph Recommendations**  \n   *Technology:* Neo4j 5.x  \n   *Rationale:* Native graph traversals for \u201cstudents who liked X also liked Y\u201d.\n\n6. **File Storage (Assignments, Media)**  \n   *Technology:* S3-compatible object store with signed URLs  \n   *Rationale:* Durable, CDN-friendly, off-loads traffic from app servers.\n\n### Access Pattern Enforcement  \n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n  subgraph Service Layer\n    SVC[Micro-service]\n  end\n  subgraph Repositories\n    REPO1[(PostgreSQL Repo)]\n    REPO2[(Redis Repo)]\n    REPO3[(Kafka Repo)]\n  end\n  SVC --> REPO1 & REPO2 & REPO3\n```\n\nRepositories shield business logic from vendor SDKs. All repositories implement:\n\n```ts\n// docs/examples/Repository.ts\nexport interface Repository<T> {\n  findById(id: string): Promise<T | null>;\n  save(entity: T): Promise<void>;\n  delete(id: string): Promise<void>;\n}\n```\n\nConcrete adapters (e.g., `UserPgRepository`, `TimelineRedisRepository`) live in their respective packages.\n\n### Data-Contracts & Async Sync  \nCross-store ownership is disallowed; instead we replicate immutable projections using Kafka topics suffixed with `.projection`. Consumers materialize local read models, guaranteeing eventual consistency while avoiding distributed transactions.\n\n## Consequences  \nPositive\n* Services scale independently; no single datastore becomes a bottleneck.\n* Teams can evolve schemas without cross-team migration battles.\n* Disaster recovery is narrowed to datastore-specific SLAs.\n\nNegative\n* Ops: multiple backup/restore, monitoring, and upgrade procedures.\n* Observability: needing distributed tracing across store boundaries.\n* Onboarding: developers must learn \u2265 3 query DSLs.\n\nMitigations\n* Unified secrets via Vault; IaC modules standardize provisioning.\n* Cross-store dashboards in Grafana/Loki/Tempo.\n* Internal workshops and cheat-sheets for new engineers.\n\n## Related Decisions  \n* ADR-001 \u2013 Event-Driven Architecture  \n* ADR-002 \u2013 Domain-Driven Repository Pattern\n\n## Notes  \nThis ADR will be revisited after the next academic year or when datastore OPEX exceeds 20 % of infrastructure budget.",
    "filePath": "/app/project/docs/ADR/003-polyglot-persistence.md",
    "numLines": 108,
    "startLine": 1,
    "totalLines": 108
  },

  "content": "# Architectural Analysis Report: User Progress Update Latency in PulseLearn Campus Hub\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThis report provides a root cause analysis of the intermittent latency (up to 60 seconds) experienced by users when their progress updates (lecture completions, quiz scores) appear on the dashboard's progress chart and activity stream. The analysis traces the complete data flow through the system, identifies critical architectural components, and pinpoints the top three most likely causes of the delay.\n\n**Key Finding:** The latency is an inherent consequence of the system's event-driven, eventually consistent architecture as defined in ADR-001 and ADR-002. The delay is not a bug but a manifestation of the trade-offs made to achieve loose coupling, fault isolation, and horizontal scalability. However, specific architectural areas can be optimized to reduce the perceived latency.\n\n---\n\n## 1. `services/payment-service/src/events/consumer.js` | Consumer pattern with retry and DLQ |\n| Event Publisher | `services/course-service/src/api/courseController.js:33` | Domain event dispatching from Top 3 Most Likely Architectural Areas Causing Delay\n\n### 3.1 Bottleneck #1: Kafka Consumer Lag Under Load\n\n**Justification:**\n\nThe event-driven architecture relies on Kafka for cross-service communication (ADR-002). The symptom of \"intermittent delay that worsens under peak usage\" is a classic indicator of **consumer lag** - where the rate of message production exceeds the consumer's processing capacity.\n\n**Evidence from Codebase:**\n\n1. **Single-Partition Configuration** (`docker-compose.yml:124`):\n   ```yaml\n   KAFKA_OFFSETS_TOPIC_REPLICATION_FACTOR: 1\n   ```\n   A replication factor of 1 in a development setup suggests a single broker with limited partition distribution. Under load, a single partition becomes a bottleneck because Kafka consumers in the same consumer group can only have one active consumer per partition.\n\n2. **Consumer Group Design** (`services/course-service/src/app.js:96`):\n   ```javascript\n   const consumer = kafka.consumer({ groupId: KAFKA_GROUP_ID });\n   ```\n   The `course-service-consumer` group ID is shared, meaning multiple service instances would compete for the same partitions rather than scaling horizontally.\n\n3. **No Explicit Partitioning Strategy** (`services/course-service/src/app.js:98-103`):\n   ```javascript\n   async function publishEvent(topic, payload) {\n     await producer.send({\n       topic,\n       messages: [{ key: payload.id || null, value: JSON.stringify(payload) }],\n     });\n   }\n   ```\n   The `key` is set to `payload.id` or `null`. When `null`, messages are round-robin distributed, but when set, they're partitioned by key. Inconsistent keying can lead to hot partitions.\n\n4. **ADR-002 Acknowledges This Trade-off**:\n   > \"Negative / Trade-offs: ... developers must understand eventual consistency.\"\n\n**Impact Analysis:**\n\nWhen many users complete lectures simultaneously (peak hours), the `LESSON_COMPLETED` events queue up in Kafka. The single consumer instance in the notification-service processes them sequentially, causing a backlog. The delay between event publication and WebSocket push directly correlates with this lag.\n\n**Metric to Monitor:** Consumer lag can be monitored via `kafka-consumer-groups.sh --describe` or Prometheus metrics (`kafka_consumer_group_lag`).\n\n---\n\n### 3.2 Bottleneck #2: Frontend Polling Strategy and Stale Cache\n\n**Justification:**\n\nThe dashboard components use multiple data retrieval strategies that are not optimally coordinated, leading to perceived latency even when the backend has the updated data.\n\n**Evidence from Codebase:**\n\n1. **No Automatic Refresh After Write** (`frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js:139-156`):\n   ```javascript\n   const fetchDashboardSnapshot = useCallback(async () => {\n     // ...\n     const snapshot = await DashboardService.getSnapshot({ token, signal });\n     setMetrics(snapshot.metrics);\n     setActivityFeed(snapshot.activity);\n     setProgressData(snapshot.progress);\n   }, [token]);\n   ```\n   This function is called only on mount (`useEffect` at line 240-252). There is **no periodic polling** and no re-fetch after the user completes an action. The dashboard relies entirely on WebSocket pushes for updates.\n\n2. **WebSocket Event Handling is Selective** (`frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js:194-221`):\n   ```javascript\n   socket.current.on('dashboard-event', (domainEvent) => {\n     switch (domainEvent.type) {\n       case 'BadgeAwarded':\n         // updates badges\n         break;\n       case 'ProgressUpdated':\n         setProgressData(domainEvent.payload.chartData);\n         break;\n       // ...\n     }\n   });\n   ```\n   The `ProgressUpdated` event must be explicitly emitted by the backend for the chart to update. If the backend's consumer chain fails to emit this event (e.g., due to consumer lag or a missed event), the chart remains stale.\n\n3. **ProgressChart Has Its Own WebSocket** (`frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js:96-100`):\n   ```javascript\n   const wsUrl = `wss://api.pulselearn.com/ws/progress/${encodeURIComponent(userId)}`;\n   const ws = new WebSocket(wsUrl);\n   ```\n   This is a **separate WebSocket connection** from the DashboardPage's Socket.io connection. The two are not synchronized. If one updates but the other doesn't, the user sees inconsistent state.\n\n4. **Frontend Service Caching** (`frontend/src/services/courseService.js:77-78`):\n   ```javascript\n   const COURSE_CACHE_TTL = 30 * 1000; // 30s\n   const courseCache = createTTLCache(COURSE_CACHE_TTL);\n   ```\n   The 30-second TTL cache means that even if a user navigates to a course details page immediately after completion, they may see stale data until the cache expires.\n\n**Impact Analysis:**\n\nA user completes a lecture, the write succeeds, but:\n1. The DashboardPage doesn't automatically re-fetch\n2. The WebSocket push may be delayed due to Kafka consumer lag\n3. Even if data is fetched, the courseService cache may return stale data\n\nThe user perceives no update for up to 60 seconds (combining consumer lag + cache TTL + WebSocket reconnection delay).\n\n---\n\n### 3.3 Bottleneck #3: Eventual Consistency and Read Model Projection Delay\n\n**Justification:**\n\nThe architecture explicitly uses **eventual consistency** with read model projections (ADR-001, ADR-002, ADR-003). The dashboard reads from materialized views that are updated asynchronously, not from the source of truth.\n\n**Evidence from Codebase:**\n\n1. **Read Models are Projections** (`docs/ADR/002-event-sourcing-with-kafka.md`):\n   > \"Append-only: write operations emit events; read models are derived via consumer projections.\"\n\n   The progress data shown on the dashboard is a **projection** (a denormalized read model) maintained by a consumer that listens to the event stream. This projection may be in a different database (Redis for timelines per ADR-003).\n\n2. **Polyglot Persistence** (`docs/ADR/003-polyglot-persistence.md`):\n   > \"Realtime Timelines & Notifications: Technology: Redis Cluster + Redis Streams. Rationale: Sub-millisecond fan-out, pub/sub semantics, TTL-based eviction.\"\n\n   The activity stream and progress chart may read from Redis projections, not PostgreSQL. The consumer that updates these projections must process the Kafka event first.\n\n3. **Cross-Store Synchronization** (`docs/ADR/003-polyglot-persistence.md:84-85`):\n   > \"Cross-store ownership is disallowed; instead we replicate immutable projections using Kafka topics suffixed with `.projection`. Consumers materialize local read models, guaranteeing eventual consistency while avoiding distributed transactions.\"\n\n4. **Consumer Projection Chain** (inferred from `services/course-service/src/app.js:127-131`):\n   ```javascript\n   async function handleAssignmentSubmitted({ courseId, studentId }) {\n     await Course.update({ updatedAt: new Date() }, { where: { id: courseId } });\n     await publishEvent('CourseProgressUpdated', { courseId, studentId, ts: Date.now() });\n   }\n   ```\n   This shows a **two-hop event chain**:\n   - `AssignmentSubmitted` \u2192 consumed by course-service\n   - `CourseProgressUpdated` \u2192 published for downstream consumers (notification-service, activity-service)\n\n   Each hop introduces latency from consumer processing and network round-trips.\n\n5. **DLQ and Retry Logic** (`services/payment-service/src/events/consumer.js:173-181`):\n   ```javascript\n   await pRetry(() => handler(data, metadata), {\n     retries: MAX_PROCESSING_RETRIES, // 5 retries\n     onFailedAttempt: (err) => {\n       logger.warn(`Attempt ${err.attemptNumber} failed...`);\n     },\n   });\n   ```\n   Retries introduce additional delays if messages fail on first attempt.\n\n**Impact Analysis:**\n\nThe total latency is the sum of:\n1. **Source write** (PostgreSQL lessonCompletion) - ~10-50ms\n2. **Event publish to Kafka** - ~5-20ms\n3. **Consumer pickup delay** (depends on lag) - 0ms to 10+ seconds under load\n4. **Projection update** (Redis/Elasticsearch write) - ~5-50ms\n5. **Secondary event publish** (CourseProgressUpdated) - ~5-20ms\n6. **Notification-service consumer pickup** - 0ms to 10+ seconds\n7. **WebSocket broadcast** - ~5-50ms\n\nUnder ideal conditions: ~50-200ms\nUnder load with consumer lag: 10-60+ seconds\n\n---\n\n## 4. Architectural Trade-off Analysis\n\nThe latency is not a defect but an **explicit trade-off** documented in the ADRs:\n\n| Trade-off | Benefit | Cost |\n|-----------|---------|------|\n| Event Sourcing (ADR-002) | Auditability, replayability, loose coupling | Eventual consistency, write complexity |\n| Microservices (ADR-001) | Independent deployability, fault isolation | Operational overhead, eventual consistency |\n| Polyglot Persistence (ADR-003) | Fit-for-purpose data stores | Cross-store synchronization delay |\n\n**Quote from ADR-001:**\n> \"Negative: ... Data consistency becomes eventual; we must adopt Saga patterns for workflows...\"\n\n**Quote from ADR-002:**\n> \"Negative / Trade-offs: ... developers must understand eventual consistency.\"\n\n---\n\n## 5. Recommendations\n\n### Short-term Mitigations (No Architecture Change)\n\n1. **Optimistic UI Updates**: After the `handleEnded()` POST returns successfully, immediately update the local React state to reflect the completion without waiting for the WebSocket push.\n\n2. **Increase Kafka Partitions**: Increase partitions for high-throughput topics to allow parallel consumption.\n\n3. **Add Periodic Polling Fallback**: Implement a 10-second polling interval in DashboardPage as a fallback when WebSocket events are delayed.\n\n4. **Reduce Frontend Cache TTL**: Reduce the courseService cache from 30s to 5-10s for progress-related endpoints.\n\n### Medium-term Optimizations\n\n1. **Consumer Scaling**: Deploy multiple instances of notification-service with unique consumer group assignments across partitions.\n\n2. **Read-Your-Writes Consistency**: After a write, include the expected version/timestamp in the response. The frontend can then poll until the read model matches this version.\n\n3. **Redis Streams for Real-time Path**: Bypass Kafka for user-facing real-time updates and use Redis Pub/Sub or Streams for sub-second delivery.\n\n### Long-term Architectural Considerations\n\n1. **CQRS Command Acknowledgment**: Implement a command/query acknowledgment pattern where the write path returns a correlation ID, and the frontend subscribes to a completion notification for that specific ID.\n\n2. **WebSocket Unification**: Consolidate the multiple WebSocket connections (Socket.io for dashboard-events, native WebSocket for ProgressChart) into a single multiplexed connection.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Conclusion\n\nThe intermittent 60-second delay in progress updates is a consequence of the PulseLearn Campus Hub's event-driven, eventually consistent architecture. The three primary bottlenecks are:\n\n1. **Kafka consumer lag** under peak load causing event processing delays\n2. **Frontend polling/caching strategy** that doesn't account for write-read latency\n3. **Multi-hop event chains** inherent in the CQRS projection pattern\n\nThese are not bugs but architectural trade-offs made to achieve scalability, fault tolerance, and loose coupling. The recommendations above provide a path to reducing perceived latency while preserving the benefits of the current architecture.\n\n---\n\n## Appendix: File Reference Summary\n\n| Purpose | File Path | Key Lines |\n|---------|-----------|-----------|\n| Write trigger | `frontend/src/components/course/LecturePlayer.js` | 181-189 |\n| Dashboard fetch | `frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js` | 139-156, 182-223 |\n| Progress chart WS | `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js` | 62-174 |\n| Activity stream | `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ActivityStream.js` | 85-208 |\n| Course service | `services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js` | 317-350, 72-93 |\n| App bootstrap | `services/course-service/src/app.js` | 96-131 |\n| Event consumer pattern | `services/payment-service/src/events/consumer.js` | 74-148 |\n| Kafka config | `docker-compose.yml` | 120-138 |\n| ADR Event Sourcing | `docs/ADR/002-event-sourcing-with-kafka.md` | Full document |\n| ADR Microservices | `docs/ADR/001-microservices-architecture.md` | Full document |\n| ADR Polyglot | `docs/ADR/003-polyglot-persistence.md` | Full document |\n",

GET /api/v1/activity-stream?page=0&size=25                         \u2502\n\u2502    - Supports infinite scroll pagination                                \u2502\n\u2502                                                                         \u2502\n\u2502  Real-Time Updates:                                                     \u2502\n\u2502    - Key Architectural Components Involved\n\n### 2.1 Frontend Layer\n\n| Component | File Path | Role |\n|-----------|-----------|------|\n| LecturePlayer | `frontend/src/components/course/LecturePlayer.js` | Triggers progress write on lecture completion |\n| DashboardPage | `frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js` | Orchestrates dashboard data fetching and WebSocket subscription |\n| ProgressChart | `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js` | Dedicated WebSocket for course completion percentages |\n| ActivityStream | `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ActivityStream.js` | Hybrid REST+WebSocket activity feed |\n| courseService | `frontend/src/services/courseService.js` | Axios HTTP client with caching (30s TTL) |\n| api.js | `frontend/src/services/api.js` | Centralized HTTP/SSE client with token refresh |\n\n### 2.2 Backend Services\n\n| Service | Port | Database | Role |\n|---------|------|----------|------|\n| API Gateway | 8080 | N/A | Nginx reverse proxy, rate limiting, SSL termination |\n| Course Service | 7002 | PostgreSQL | Course CRUD, progress tracking, event publishing |\n| Notification Service | 7003 | Redis | WebSocket push, email delivery |\n| Activity Service | 7002 | PostgreSQL | Activity stream read model |\n| User Service | 7001 | PostgreSQL | Authentication, profiles |\n\n### 2.3 Infrastructure Components\n\n| Component | Technology | Configuration File |\n|-----------|------------|-------------------|\n| Message Broker | Kafka 7.5.0 + Zookeeper | `docker-compose.yml:106-138` |\n| Message Broker (secondary) | NATS 2.10 JetStream | `docker-compose.yml:141-151` |\n| Primary Database | PostgreSQL 15 | `docker-compose.yml:75-90` |\n| Cache | Redis 7 | `docker-compose.yml:92-104` |\n| Search | Elasticsearch 8.11.1 | `docker-compose.yml:153-168` |\n| Object Storage | MinIO | `docker-compose.yml:183-197` |\n\n### 2.4 Critical Code `services/payment-service/src/events/consumer.js` | Consumer pattern with retry and DLQ |\n| Event Publisher | `services/course-service/src/api/courseController.js:33` | Domain event dispatching from controller |\n\n---\n\n## 3. Top 3 Most Likely Architectural Areas Causing Delay\n\n### 3.1 Bottleneck #1: Kafka Consumer Lag Under Load\n\n**Justification:**\n\nThe event-driven architecture relies on Kafka for cross-service communication (ADR-002). The symptom of \"intermittent delay that worsens under peak usage\" is a classic indicator of **consumer lag** - where the rate of message production exceeds the consumer's processing capacity.\n\n**Evidence from Codebase:**\n\n1. **Single-Partition Configuration** (`docker-compose.yml:124`):\n   ```yaml\n   KAFKA_OFFSETS_TOPIC_REPLICATION_FACTOR: 1\n   ```\n   A replication factor of 1 in a development setup suggests a single broker with limited partition distribution. Under load, a single partition becomes a bottleneck because Kafka consumers in the same consumer group can only have one active consumer per partition.\n\n2. **Consumer Group Design** (`services/course-service/src/app.js:96`):\n   ```javascript\n   const consumer = kafka.consumer({ groupId: KAFKA_GROUP_ID });\n   ```\n   The `course-service-consumer` group ID is shared, meaning multiple service instances would compete for the same partitions rather than scaling horizontally.\n\n3. **No Explicit Partitioning Strategy** (`services/course-service/src/app.js:98-103`):\n   ```javascript\n   async function publishEvent(topic, payload) {\n     await producer.send({\n       topic,\n       messages: [{ key: payload.id || null, value: JSON.stringify(payload) }],\n     });\n   }\n   ```\n   The `key` is set to `payload.id` or `null`. When `null`, messages are round-robin distributed, but when set, they're partitioned by key. Inconsistent keying can lead to hot partitions.\n\n4. **ADR-002 Acknowledges This Trade-off**:\n   > \"Negative / Trade-offs: ... developers must understand eventual consistency.\"\n\n**Impact Analysis:**\n\nWhen many users complete lectures simultaneously (peak hours), the `LESSON_COMPLETED` events queue up in Kafka. The single consumer instance in the notification-service processes them sequentially, causing a backlog. The delay between event publication and WebSocket push directly correlates with this lag.\n\n**Metric to Monitor:** Consumer lag can be monitored via `kafka-consumer-groups.sh --describe` or Prometheus metrics (`kafka_consumer_group_lag`).\n\n---\n\n### 3.2 Bottleneck #2: Frontend Polling Strategy and Stale Cache\n\n**Justification:**\n\nThe dashboard components use multiple data retrieval strategies that are not optimally coordinated, leading to perceived latency even when the backend has the updated data.\n\n**Evidence from Codebase:**\n\n1. **No Automatic Refresh After Write** (`frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js:139-156`):\n   ```javascript\n   const fetchDashboardSnapshot = useCallback(async () => {\n     // ...\n     const snapshot = await DashboardService.getSnapshot({ token, signal });\n     setMetrics(snapshot.metrics);\n     setActivityFeed(snapshot.activity);\n     setProgressData(snapshot.progress);\n   }, [token]);\n   ```\n   This function is called only on mount (`useEffect` at line 240-252). There is **no periodic polling** and no re-fetch after the user completes an action. The dashboard relies entirely on WebSocket pushes for updates.\n\n2. **WebSocket Event Handling is Selective** (`frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js:194-221`):\n   ```javascript\n   socket.current.on('dashboard-event', (domainEvent) => {\n     switch (domainEvent.type) {\n       case 'BadgeAwarded':\n         // updates badges\n         break;\n       case 'ProgressUpdated':\n         setProgressData(domainEvent.payload.chartData);\n         break;\n       // ...\n     }\n   });\n   ```\n   The `ProgressUpdated` event must be explicitly emitted by the backend for the chart to update. If the backend's consumer chain fails to emit this event (e.g., due to consumer lag or a missed event), the chart remains stale.\n\n3. **ProgressChart Has Its Own WebSocket** (`frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js:96-100`):\n   ```javascript\n   const wsUrl = `wss://api.pulselearn.com/ws/progress/${encodeURIComponent(userId)}`;\n   const ws = new WebSocket(wsUrl);\n   ```\n   This is a **separate WebSocket connection** from the DashboardPage's Socket.io connection. The two are not synchronized. If one updates but the other doesn't, the user sees inconsistent state.\n\n4. **Frontend Service Caching** (`frontend/src/services/courseService.js:77-78`):\n   ```javascript\n   const COURSE_CACHE_TTL = 30 * 1000; // 30s\n   const courseCache = createTTLCache(COURSE_CACHE_TTL);\n   ```\n   The 30-second TTL cache means that even if a user navigates to a course details page immediately after completion, they may see stale data until the cache expires.\n\n**Impact Analysis:**\n\nA user completes a lecture, the write succeeds, but:\n1. The DashboardPage doesn't automatically re-fetch\n2. The WebSocket push may be delayed due to Kafka consumer lag\n3. Even if data is fetched, the courseService cache may return stale data\n\nThe user perceives no update for up to 60 seconds (combining consumer lag + cache TTL + WebSocket reconnection delay).\n\n---\n\n### 3.3 Bottleneck #3: Eventual Consistency and Read Model Projection Delay\n\n**Justification:**\n\nThe architecture explicitly uses **eventual consistency** with read model projections (ADR-001, ADR-002, ADR-003). The dashboard reads from materialized views that are updated asynchronously, not from the source of truth.\n\n**Evidence from Codebase:**\n\n1. **Read Models are Projections** (`docs/ADR/002-event-sourcing-with-kafka.md`):\n   > \"Append-only: write operations emit events; read models are derived via consumer projections.\"\n\n   The progress data shown on the dashboard is a **projection** (a denormalized read model) maintained by a consumer that listens to the event stream. This projection may be in a different database (Redis for timelines per ADR-003).\n\n2. **Polyglot Persistence** (`docs/ADR/003-polyglot-persistence.md`):\n   > \"Realtime Timelines & Notifications: Technology: Redis Cluster + Redis Streams. Rationale: Sub-millisecond fan-out, pub/sub semantics, TTL-based eviction.\"\n\n   The activity stream and progress chart may read from Redis projections, not PostgreSQL. The consumer that updates these projections must process the Kafka event first.\n\n3. **Cross-Store Synchronization** (`docs/ADR/003-polyglot-persistence.md:84-85`):\n   > \"Cross-store ownership is disallowed; instead we replicate immutable projections using Kafka topics suffixed with `.projection`. Consumers materialize local read models, guaranteeing eventual consistency while avoiding distributed transactions.\"\n\n4. **Consumer Projection Chain** (inferred from `services/course-service/src/app.js:127-131`):\n   ```javascript\n   async function handleAssignmentSubmitted({ courseId, studentId }) {\n     await Course.update({ updatedAt: new Date() }, { where: { id: courseId } });\n     await publishEvent('CourseProgressUpdated', { courseId, studentId, ts: Date.now() });\n   }\n   ```\n   This shows a **two-hop event chain**:\n   - `AssignmentSubmitted` \u2192 consumed by course-service\n   - `CourseProgressUpdated` \u2192 published for downstream consumers (notification-service, activity-service)\n\n   Each hop introduces latency from consumer processing and network round-trips.\n\n5. **DLQ and Retry Logic** (`services/payment-service/src/events/consumer.js:173-181`):\n   ```javascript\n   await pRetry(() => handler(data, metadata), {\n     retries: MAX_PROCESSING_RETRIES, // 5 retries\n     onFailedAttempt: (err) => {\n       logger.warn(`Attempt ${err.attemptNumber} failed...`);\n     },\n   });\n   ```\n   Retries introduce additional delays if messages fail on first attempt.\n\n**Impact Analysis:**\n\nThe total latency is the sum of:\n1. **Source write** (PostgreSQL lessonCompletion) - ~10-50ms\n2. **Event publish to Kafka** - ~5-20ms\n3. **Consumer pickup delay** (depends on lag) - 0ms to 10+ seconds under load\n4. **Projection update** (Redis/Elasticsearch write) - ~5-50ms\n5. **Secondary event publish** (CourseProgressUpdated) - ~5-20ms\n6. **Notification-service consumer pickup** - 0ms to 10+ seconds\n7. **WebSocket broadcast** - ~5-50ms\n\nUnder ideal conditions: ~50-200ms\nUnder load with consumer lag: 10-60+ seconds\n\n---\n\n## 4. Architectural Trade-off Analysis\n\nThe latency is not a defect but an **explicit trade-off** documented in the ADRs:\n\n| Trade-off | Benefit | Cost |\n|-----------|---------|------|\n| Event Sourcing (ADR-002) | Auditability, replayability, loose coupling | Eventual consistency, write complexity |\n| Microservices (ADR-001) | Independent deployability, fault isolation | Operational overhead, eventual consistency |\n| Polyglot Persistence (ADR-003) | Fit-for-purpose data stores | Cross-store synchronization delay |\n\n**Quote from ADR-001:**\n> \"Negative: ... Data consistency becomes eventual; we must adopt Saga patterns for workflows...\"\n\n**Quote from ADR-002:**\n> \"Negative / Trade-offs: ... developers must understand eventual consistency.\"\n\n---\n\n## 5. Recommendations\n\n### Short-term Mitigations (No Architecture Change)\n\n1. **Optimistic UI Updates**: After the `handleEnded()` POST returns successfully, immediately update the local React state to reflect the completion without waiting for the WebSocket push.\n\n2. **Increase Kafka Partitions**: Increase partitions for high-throughput topics to allow parallel consumption.\n\n3. **Add Periodic Polling Fallback**: Implement a 10-second polling interval in DashboardPage as a fallback when WebSocket events are delayed.\n\n4. **Reduce Frontend Cache TTL**: Reduce the courseService cache from 30s to 5-10s for progress-related endpoints.\n\n### Medium-term Optimizations\n\n1. **Consumer Scaling**: Deploy multiple instances of notification-service with unique consumer group assignments across partitions.\n\n2. **Read-Your-Writes Consistency**: After a write, include the expected version/timestamp in the response. The frontend can then poll until the read model matches this version.\n\n3. **Redis Streams for Real-time Path**: Bypass Kafka for user-facing real-time updates and use Redis Pub/Sub or Streams for sub-second delivery.\n\n### Long-term Architectural Considerations\n\n1. **CQRS Command Acknowledgment**: Implement a command/query acknowledgment pattern where the write path returns a correlation ID, and the frontend subscribes to a completion notification for that specific ID.\n\n2. **WebSocket Unification**: Consolidate the multiple WebSocket connections (Socket.io for dashboard-events, native WebSocket for ProgressChart) into a single multiplexed connection.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Conclusion\n\nThe intermittent 60-second delay in progress updates is a consequence of the PulseLearn Campus Hub's event-driven, eventually consistent architecture. The three primary bottlenecks are:\n\n1. **Kafka consumer lag** under peak load causing event processing delays\n2. **Frontend polling/caching strategy** that doesn't account for write-read latency\n3. **Multi-hop event chains** inherent in the CQRS projection pattern\n\nThese are not bugs but architectural trade-offs made to achieve scalability, fault tolerance, and loose coupling. The recommendations above provide a path to reducing perceived latency while preserving the benefits of the current architecture.\n\n---\n\n## Appendix: File Reference Summary\n\n| Purpose | File Path | Key Lines |\n|---------|-----------|-----------|\n| Write trigger | `frontend/src/components/course/LecturePlayer.js` | 181-189 |\n| Dashboard fetch | `frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js` | 139-156, 182-223 |\n| Progress chart WS | `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js` | 62-174 |\n| Activity stream | `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ActivityStream.js` | 85-208 |\n| Course service | `services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js` | 317-350, 72-93 |\n| App bootstrap | `services/course-service/src/app.js` | 96-131 |\n| Event consumer pattern | `services/payment-service/src/events/consumer.js` | 74-148 |\n| Kafka config | `docker-compose.yml` | 120-138 |\n| ADR Event Sourcing | `docs/ADR/002-event-sourcing-with-kafka.md` | Full document |\n| ADR Microservices | `docs/ADR/001-microservices-architecture.md` | Full document |\n| ADR Polyglot | `docs/ADR/003-polyglot-persistence.md` | Full document |\n",

# Architectural Analysis Report: User Progress Update Latency in PulseLearn Campus Hub

## Executive Summary

This report provides a root cause analysis of the intermittent latency (up to 60 seconds) experienced by users when their progress updates (lecture completions, quiz scores) appear on the dashboard's progress chart and activity stream. The analysis traces the complete data flow through the system, identifies critical architectural components, and pinpoints the top three most likely causes of the delay.

**Key Finding:** The latency is an inherent consequence of the system's event-driven, eventually consistent architecture as defined in ADR-001 and ADR-002. The delay is not a bug but a manifestation of the trade-offs made to achieve loose coupling, fault isolation, and horizontal scalability. However, specific architectural areas can be optimized to reduce the perceived latency.

---

## 1. End-to-End Data Flow Analysis

The user progress update flow consists of three distinct paths that operate on different timescales:

### 1.1 The Write Path (Synchronous)

When a user completes a lecture, the following synchronous sequence occurs:

```
User Action (LecturePlayer.js)
    │
    ▼
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  FRONTEND (Synchronous API Calls)                                       │
│  File: frontend/src/components/course/LecturePlayer.js:181-189          │
│                                                                         │
│  1. handleEnded() triggers when video ends                              │
│  2. Emits 'LectureCompleted' event to local eventBus                    │
│  3. POSTs to /courses/${courseId}/lectures/${lectureId}/complete        │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
... (truncated)
